Foreword
⚫

Machine learning is a key pathway for implementing AI. Within machine learning,

deep learning stands out as a crucial branch, underpinning fields such as computer
vision (CV), speech recognition, and natural language processing (NLP). Deep learning
is based on the research of artificial neural networks. This lesson introduces you to
the structure of neural network models and their training methods.

Addressing Insufficiency of Training Data
⚫

Insufficiency of training data: there is not enough data to train a model.

⚫

Solution: data augmentation. Data augmentation aims to increase the diversity and size of the training
dataset by applying a variety of transformations to existing data. These transformations mimic real-world

changes, enriching the training dataset. The specific methods vary depending on the tasks at hand.


Commonly used image data augmentation methods: zooming, stretching, adding noise, flipping, rotation,
translation, shearing, contrast adjustment, and channel transformation.



Commonly used data augmentation methods for NLP: sentence paraphrasing, synonym replacement, back
translation, and EDA.



Commonly used data augmentation methods for audio: cropping, rotation, changing the pitch and tone, adding
noise, and SpecAugment.

9

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• EDA consists of four simple but powerful operations: synonym replacement, random
insertion, random swap, and random deletion.
• Data augmentation is a necessary step for training deep learning models. It is generally
effective in improving the generalization capability of models. Pay attention to the
following:
▫ Typically, you double the size of the original dataset through data augmentation.
Increasing the dataset size by 10 or even 100 times solely to extend the training
duration won't further improve the model's generalization capability.
▫ Do not add irrelevant data.

Underfitting and Overfitting
⚫

Underfitting occurs when a machine learning model is too simple to capture the underlying patterns in the training
data, leading to high loss function values.

⚫

Overfitting occurs when the model cannot generalize and fits too closely to the training data.

Underfitting
Failed to learn features

10

y

Good fitting

x
Overfitting

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Differences between underfitting and overfitting: Underfitting means that your model has
poor performance on both of the training and test sets. Overfitting means that your model
performs excellently on the training set but poorly on the test set. In neural network
training, the output of an underfitted model usually exhibits high bias, while the output of
an overfitted model typically has high variance.

Causes and Fixes of Underfitting
⚫

⚫

Causes of underfitting:


The model is trained on insufficient features.



The model is not complex enough to learn hidden patterns from data.

How to fix underfitting:

11



Add new features. You can add feature combinations and high-order features to increase the hypothesis space.



Add polynomial features. This method is widely used in machine learning algorithms. For example, you can add quadratic or
cubic items to a linear model to enhance the model's generalization capability.



Reduce regularization parameters. Regularization is used to prevent overfitting. If underfitting occurs, it might be necessary to
reduce the regularization parameters.



Use non-linear models, such as kernel SVM, decision tree, and deep learning models.



Adjust the model's capacity. Generally, a model's capacity is its ability to fit a variety of functions.



Low-capacity models may struggle to capture hidden patterns in the training data. To solve this, you may consider using
ensemble learning methods, such as boosting, which integrates multiple weak learners into one strong learner.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Dropout
⚫

Dropout randomly disables some neurons during training, whereby the parameters of these disabled
neurons will not participate in the next round of training. This allows the remaining neurons to learn
better.

⚫

The complete neural network is used during testing. Dropout is similar to bagging in that both are
techniques used to reduce overfitting.

Machine Learning Tasks
⚫

⚫

The following are typical machine learning tasks:


Classification: The model outputs discrete class labels. For instance, image classification in the domain of
computer vision is a classification task.



Regression: The model outputs a continuous quantity. One example of this task is predicting the future claims
amount by policyholders, allowing insurance companies to set appropriate insurance premiums. Another
example is predicting the future prices of securities.



Clustering: Based on internal similarities, a large amount of unlabeled data can be grouped into multiple classes.
Data in the same class share more similarities than data from different classes. Examples of clustering tasks
include search by image and user profiling.



Generation: This type of task generates things based on its input. It can output vectors, matrixes, sequences, and
others. Examples of this type of task include machine translation and speech recognition.

Classification and regression are two major types of prediction tasks. Classification outputs discrete class
labels, while regression outputs a continuous set.

14

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Machine Learning Methods (1)
⚫

Supervised learning: Uses labeled datasets to train algorithms or models to make predictions or
recognize patterns. During the training, algorithms/models learn the relationship between features in
the datasets and the target.

⚫

Unsupervised learning: Analyzes unlabeled datasets to discover patterns without human supervision.

⚫

Self-supervised learning: Trains a model on unlabeled data, generates supervisory signals (labels)
automatically, and continues training on the remaining data. This is a relatively new machine learning
method.

⚫

The term "supervised" in supervised learning means that the supervisor teaches the machines what to

do by feeding them labeled data. In unsupervised learning, algorithms must learn hidden patterns in
training data without supervision.

15

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Machine Learning Methods (2)
⚫

Supervised learning and non-supervised learning are not exclusive to each other. Many machine learning
algorithms use them together.

⚫

Semi-supervised learning: Uses the combination of a small amount of labeled data and a large amount

of unlabeled data to train a model. It is a method that falls in between supervised and unsupervised
learning.

⚫

Reinforcement learning: Reinforcement learning is about learning the optimal behavior in an
environment to obtain maximum reward. Reinforcement learning does not require labeled data or a

training set. It relies on the ability to monitor the response to the actions of the learning agent. Instead
of being given the correct answer, the learning agent learns the optimal answer from continuous reward
feedback.
16

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• There are two popular methods for semi-supervised learning. One is to perform
unsupervised clustering first, followed by supervised learning. The other is self-learning.

Challenges in Traditional Machine Learning
⚫

Curse of dimensionality: As the dimensionality of data (the number of features) increases, the
number of data points needed for any machine learning algorithms to have good performance
increases exponentially, which also means an exponential increase in computational costs.

17

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Due to limited capacity, traditional machine learning models often struggle with highdimensional training data. This means necessary feature extraction and selection are
sometimes required.
• Traditional machine learning models often have limitations in many types of tasks.

Biological Neuron vs. Artificial Neuron
⚫

The human brain consists of more than 100 billion cells known as neurons. The function of a
neuron is to receive (dendrite), integrate (cell body or soma), conduct (axon), and output (axon
terminal) information.

• Biological neurons have two key characteristics: excitability and conductivity.
• Neuron types (by function): sensory neuron, motor neuron, and interneuron.
• Sensory neurons (input neurons in an artificial neural network) are neurons in the nervous
system, that convert a specific type of stimulus, via their receptors, into action potentials or
graded potentials. This process is called sensory transduction. The cell bodies of the sensory
neurons are located in the dorsal ganglia of the spinal cord.
• Motor neurons (output neurons in an artificial neural network) are neurons whose cell
bodies are located in the motor cortex, brainstem or the spinal cord, and whose axon
(fiber) projects to the spinal cord or outside of the spinal cord to directly or indirectly
control effector organs, mainly muscles and glands. The excitement of motor neurons
drives the activities of muscles and glands.
• Interneurons, which are found only in the central nervous system (CNS), connect one
neuron to another. They receive information from other neurons (either sensory neurons
or interneurons) and transmit information to other neurons (either motor neurons or
interneurons).

Artificial Neural Network

An artificial neural network is an attempt to simulate the network of neurons that make up the human brain so that
the computer will be able to learn things and make decisions in a humanlike manner. An artificial neural network
uses different layers of mathematical processing to make sense of the information it is fed.

History of Deep Learning
⚫

1957: Frank Rosenblatt proposes the perceptron.

⚫

1969: Minsky and Papert show that the perceptron can't solve the XOR problem.

⚫

1980: Multilayer perceptron (MLP) is proposed.

⚫

1986: Hinton proposes the backpropagation algorithm.

⚫

1989: George Cybenko invents the universal approximation theorem (why there are so many hidden layers).

⚫

2006: Hinton promotes restricted Boltzmann machines.

⚫

2009: GPUs are used to train neural networks.

⚫

2012: Convolutional neural networks achieve rapid development after AlexNet proposed by Hinton's research team becomes the
winner of ILSVRC 2012.

⚫

2016: AlphaGo beats the Go world champion Lee Sedol by 4-1. This kick-starts the rapid development of deep learning.

⚫

2022: OpenAI launches GPT-3.5. Its chatbot, ChatGPT, quickly kicks off a global frenzy over large language models, drawing
worldwide attention from both academia and industry.

⚫

2024: OpenAI launches Sora, a text-to-video model capable of generating high-quality video from text input.

22

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In fact, neural networks are not something new. The perceptron, the predecessor of neural
networks, was proposed in as early as 1957.
• After 1989, the multi-layer perceptron was very unpopular. Any paper that mentioned it
was highly likely to be rejected. So people working on it came up with a solution: changing
the name to "neural network" and "deep learning."
• The restricted Boltzmann machine (RBM) was proposed in 1986, but remained little known
until around 2006 when Hinton proposed a much faster learning procedure. In fact, the
promotion of the restricted Boltzmann machine in 2006 was more like a "stone soup" story,
acting as a catalyst that brought neural networks back to the public's view. Subsequent
research also proved that RBM initialization was in fact not very effective.

Perceptron
⚫

In 1957, the American psychologist Frank Rosenblatt proposed the Perceptron. A perceptron takes in some
numerical inputs along with weights and a bias. It then multiplies these inputs with the respective weights
(weighted sum). These products are then added together along with the bias. The activation function takes the
weighted sum and the bias as input and returns a final output. The output determines whether each neuron should
be activated or not.

⚫

A single-layer perceptron is essentially a simple binary classifier.

XOR Problem
⚫

The XOR problem is the problem of using a neural network to predict the outputs of XOR logic gates given two
binary inputs. If the two inputs are not equal, the output is 1; otherwise, the output is 0.

⚫

Being a linear model, the single-layer perceptron cannot solve non-linearly separable problems like XOR.

⚫

In 1969, Marvin Minsky, an American mathematician and pioneer in AI, claimed in his book that the perceptron is
essentially a linear model capable of handling linear classification only.

1

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• A perceptron is also referred to as a single-layer artificial neural network. This is to
differentiate from a multilayer perceptron, which is more complex. As a linear classifier, a
single-layer perceptron is the simplest form of a forward artificial neural network. Despite
its simple structure, the perceptron can solve fairly complex problems. The most
fundamental limitation of the perceptron is its inability to solve linearly inseparable
problems.
• A single-layer perceptron can only be used for linear classification. So what's linear? What's
linear classification? Linear classification is a task that uses a plane or hyperplane to classify
a set of data points into one of two discrete classes based on the value of a linear
combination of characteristics. The operation of a linear classifier cannot be visualized in
the case of a hyperplane.
• This is why we need to use a multilayer perceptron to solve nonlinear classification
problems. We need to add additional hidden layers between the input and output layers.
Within each hidden layer, each neuron always has straight lines connected to it. By adding
multiple neurons to a hidden layer, the perceptron is able to solve non-linear classification
problems.

Solving the XOR Problem: Multilayer Perceptron
⚫

Single-layer perceptrons can only classify linearly separable vectors. But if we connect many
perceptrons together, like neurons in the human brain, we can have a wide variety of nonlinear
curved planes.

Fully-Connected Neural Networks
⚫

Fully connected neural networks are among the simplest types of neural networks on which neurons are
arranged hierarchically. Each neuron is connected only to neurons at a previous layer. There is no
connection between neurons on the same layer. Information transmission in such a neural network is
one-way: from the first layer to the last.

• The functions of a single neuron are simple, and many neurons need to work together to
perform a complex task. An artificial neural network, or ANN, is a computational model
inspired by biological neural networks. It mimics the way biological neurons work in the
human brain. An ANN consists of an input layer, a variable number of hidden layers, and an
output layer.

The more layers a neural network has, the greater its ability to represent features and classify

Expansion of a Neural Network
⚫

The neural network expands the perceptron model in the following aspects:


Hidden layers: A neural network can have multiple hidden layers, which improves its ability to
represent features.



The output layer can have more than one neuron, so that the neural network can output multiple
values. This neural network can be used for more flexible classification and regression needs, as well
as dimensionality reduction and clustering.

• If no activation functions are added, the neural network is linear. In this case, regardless of
how many hidden layers are added, only one is used. Activation functions need to be added
to make the neural network non-linear.

Activation Function — Sigmoid
⚫

Closely resembling the behavior of biological neurons, the sigmoid function generates values that
increase monotonically within a defined range. It is continuous everywhere. The network can converge
better. Additionally, the output range of (0, 1) makes it especially useful for models that predict
probabilities, or for input normalization. However, the derivative of the sigmoid function approaches 0 at
places that are far away from the central point. Typically, in a network that uses sigmoid, the gradient
decreases to 0 within five layers.
Sigmoid function
1

𝑓 𝑥 =

1
1 + 𝑒 −𝑥

0.5

0
-5
33

0

5

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The sigmoid function generates values that increase monotonically within a defined range.
It is continuous everywhere. The network can converge better. However, we see that the
derivative of the sigmoid function is close to 0 at places that are far away from the central
point. When the network is very deep, more and more backpropagation gradients fall into
the saturation area, leading to increasingly smaller gradients. Typically, in a network that
uses sigmoid, the gradient decreases to 0 within five layers, making the network difficult to
train. This phenomenon is referred to as the vanishing gradient problem. In addition, the
output of the sigmoid function is not zero-centered.

Activation Function — Tanh
⚫

Tanh activation function: The average of its outputs is closer to 0 than the sigmoid function.
This allows it to converge faster than sigmoid, and the number of iterations is reduced. The
tanh activation function also suffers the problem of vanishing gradients.
tanh function

5

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The tanh function and sigmoid function have similar shortcomings. The derivative of the
tanh function is almost 0 at places far away from the center. However, because the tanh
function is symmetric with respect to the origin, the average of the outputs is closer to 0
than that of the sigmoid function. Stochastic gradient descent (SGD) can reduce the
required number of iterations because it is closer to the natural gradient descent.

Activation Function — ReLU
⚫

Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) activation function:


Advantages:
◼

The implementation is simple, computational workload is small, and

convergence is fast.
◼

ReLU eases the vanishing gradient problem.

𝑦=ቊ

35

𝑥, 𝑥 ≥ 0
0, 𝑥 < 0

𝑅𝑒𝐿𝑈 𝑥 = max(0, 𝑥)

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Advantages:
▫ In terms of biological neural networks, only 1% to 4% of the neurons are active at any
one time in the human brain. The sigmoid activation function results in a neural
network where neurons are not sparsely distributed. With good absorbability, the
ReLU function can have around 50% neurons in active state.
▫ Compared to the sigmoid function that saturates on both ends, the ReLU function
saturates only on the left side. When x > 0, the derivative of the ReLU function is 1.
Therefore, the ReLU function suffers less from the vanishing gradient problem and
accelerates the convergence rate of gradient descent.
• Disadvantages: ReLU neurons can die relatively easily. During training, if parameters are not
properly updated, a ReLU neuron in the first hidden layer may not be activated on all
training data. In this case, the parameter gradient of the neuron will always be 0 from that
point on, and the neuron will never be activated in the subsequent training process. This is
called the dying ReLU problem, which may also occur in other hidden layers.

Activation Function — Softplus and Leaky ReLU
⚫

Softplus: On top of ReLU, Softplus adds a bit computational complexity. But with a continuous
derivative, it can converge smoothly.

⚫

Leaky ReLU: Some negative values are retained so that not all information of the negative axis is
lost.

Activation Function — Softmax
⚫

Softmax function:

The softmax function is used to map a K-dimensional vector of arbitrary real values to a Kdimensional vector of real values, where each vector element is in the range (0, 1), and all the
elements add up to 1.

⚫

The softmax function is often used at the output layer of a multi-class classification task.

37

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Factors to Consider When Designing Activation Functions
⚫

Nonlinearity: When the activation function is nonlinear, a two-layer neural network can approximate any general
function. If the nonlinearity is lost, the entire network is equivalent to a single-layer linear model.

⚫

Continuous differentiability: This attribute is necessary for gradient-based optimization. If some functions that
cannot be differentiated locally are selected, their derivatives must be forcibly defined.

⚫

Boundedness: If the activation function is bounded, gradient-based training is typically more stable. If the activation
function is unbounded, the training is usually more efficient but easy to diverge. In this case, slightly reduce the
learning rate.

⚫

Monotonicity: If the activation function is monotonic, the loss function associated with the single-layer model is
convex.

⚫

Smoothness: Smooth functions with monotonic derivatives have been shown to have a better generalization
performance in some cases.

means of forward
propagation.

Compute the distance
between the

values using a loss
function.

Update learnable
parameters by using

algorithms to minimize
the loss value.

The model reaches

Iterative training

40

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• A neural network has a large number of parameters to learn, including the weight (W) and
bias (b) of each neuron.
▫ First a random value is assigned to each parameter.
▫ Then the loss function values are calculated on the training set, and parameters are
adjusted continuously to minimize the loss function. This learning process is called
optimization.
• Typically, gradient descent is used as the optimization algorithm in neural networks.

Loss Function
⚫

The loss function is sometimes used interchangeably with the term error function or cost
function.


The loss function measures the distance between a model's predictions and the actual target values.



The values of a typical loss function are negatively correlated with the degree of matching between
the predicted and the true values. If the formula uses positive correlation, add a minus sign (–) when
defining the loss function.

⚫

The purpose of training a neural network on a dataset is to tune the model parameters to
minimize the loss function.

41

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Common Loss Functions Used in Deep Learning
⚫

Cross-entropy loss measures the distance between two probability distributions. It is a loss
function widely used for classification problems.

⚫

Generally, the mean squared error (MSE) is used for regression problems, and cross-entropy
error is used for classification problems.

Extrema of a Loss Function
⚫

The loss function 𝐸(𝑊) is defined in the weight
space. Its goal is to search for the weight vector 𝑊
that minimizes the loss.

⚫

Challenge: In mathematics, there is no effective
method to find the extrema for high dimensional
1
spaces: 𝐸 𝑊 = 2𝑛 ∑𝑛𝑖=1(𝑓 𝑥𝑖 − 𝑦𝑖 )2

⚫

Solution: The function decreases most rapidly in
the opposite direction of the gradient. We can start
from a certain point and move along the −𝛻𝐸(𝑊)
direction to find the minima point. This is the core
idea behind the gradient descent method.

⚫

An analogy for gradient descent: going down a hill blindfolded.

43

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Opposite direction of
the gradient

Gradient Descent (1)
⚫

Gradient descent is about calculating the partial derivatives (gradient) of the loss function. The
gradient indicates the direction of the steepest ascent. Therefore, all parameters can be
updated by moving in the direction of steepest descent. The learning rate is an important

hyperparameter for gradient descent that determines the step size taken to adjust the weight
based on the error gradient. This parameter is represented using 𝜂.
𝑤′ = 𝑤 − 𝜂 ∗
⚫

𝜕𝐿𝑜𝑠𝑠
𝜕𝑤

The goal is to minimize the loss by updating all learnable parameters of the model based on the
learning rate (LR) and gradient

44

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• How do we move from the initial position to an extremum point?
▫ For each step, we move for a distance along the direction of the steepest descent.
• The gradient indicates the direction of the steepest ascent. All parameters should be
updated by moving in the opposite direction.
▫ Derivative: It tells us the slope of the function at a particular point, and along which
direction we should adjust the parameters to minimize the loss function.
▫ Directional derivative: rate of change that a function moves in any direction. (There
can be multiple directional derivatives.)

▫ Maximum directional derivative: gradient.
• Step: the step size for updating model parameters in the direction of the negative gradient
of the loss function.

Gradient Descent (2)
⚫

Different random starting points may reach different minima.

⚫

The result of each training process of the same neural network may be different.

⚫

As long as the final loss value falls within a valid range and the predefined performance metrics
are met, the result is considered valid.

45

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Gradient Descent (3)
⚫

Depending on the batch size, there are three commonly used gradient descent methods:


Batch gradient descent (BGD): For BGD, all training data is used for each update to minimize the loss function. If
there is only one minimum value, the batch gradient descent considers all data in the training set. However, if

there are too many samples, the weight update speed will be slow.


Stochastic gradient descent (SGD): For SGD, only one sample is considered during each update. Training is
accelerated but the function does not necessarily move towards minima. In addition, SGD is more sensitive to
noise.



Mini-batch gradient descent (MBGD): For MBGD, a specified number of samples (batch size) are considered
during each update. MBGD solves not only the problem of slow training speed of BGD, but also the noise

sensitivity problem in SGD.

46

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Backpropagation Algorithm (1)
⚫

Backpropagation, short for "backward propagation of errors", is an important algorithm used in neural
networks. We already know that the parameters of a model can be updated through gradient descent.
However, because there are many layers in the neural network, heavy computations are required in
order to calculate the partial derivatives of a loss function based on the chain rule. Backpropagation
avoids redundant computations of intermediate terms in the chain rule by means of dynamic
programming.


⚫

A mature deep learning framework, such as TensorFlow, automatically performs backpropagation and derivative
computation. When using such a framework, we only need to define forward operations.

Steps:

47



Back propagate the loss to each compute unit.



Each compute unit updates the weight according to the obtained errors.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Backpropagation Algorithm (2)
⚫

Backpropagation is a crucial algorithm used in neural networks. It uses the chain rule to propagate errors
from the output layer back through the network, enabling the weights of the neural network to be
updated effectively using gradient calculations.

Backpropagation

• If we use the gradient descent algorithm to optimize the model by directly using the final
loss function value, that is, tune the parameters to minimize the loss function: The
parameters are nested layer by layer. The process of calculating the gradient is complex
and the computational workload is heavy. In this case, we use the backpropagation
algorithm, which provides a method for calculating the loss function gradient backward. By
using this method, the forward errors are back propagated to each neuron and parameters
are updated using the gradient descent.
• Forward propagation means input data is fed through a network, in a forward direction, to
generate an output; and backpropagation means backward propagation of errors.

• The backpropagation algorithm provides a method for calculating the lost function gradient.
• Backpropagation process: Errors are transmitted to each compute unit (neurons at the
hidden layers) based on the weight ratio to determine the responsibility of each neuron for
the final error. Then, the weight is updated according to the allocated error.

the loss
function.

c. Perform
backpropagation to
update parameters.

Disadvantages of Gradient Descent
⚫

⚫

Convergence is not guaranteed.


A small learning rate can lead to slow convergence, while a large learning rate may cause the model to overshoot the
minimum.



The model is likely to get trapped in local minima or saddle points.

Vanishing gradient and exploding gradient


1

Vanishing gradient: When the activation function is sigmoid, the maximum value of 𝜎 ′ (𝑧) is 4 , while the initial
1

weight |𝑤| is generally less than 1. Hence, |𝜎 ′ 𝑧 𝑤| ≤ 4 . When using the chain rule, the value becomes smaller as
the number of layers increases, eventually leading to the vanishing gradient problem.


Exploding gradient: 𝑓 ′ 𝑧 𝑤 > 1 . That is, the exploding gradient problem occurs when the value of 𝑤 is large.
However, since we typically choose a small initial value, exploding gradient is not very common. In addition, the
problem can be mitigated effectively with simple gradient clipping.

50

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Causes of the vanishing gradient problem:
▫ The network is deep.
▫ An inappropriate loss function, such as sigmoid, is used.
• Exploding gradient: Generally, this problem occurs in deep networks where the initialized
weight values are too large.

Optimizer
⚫

There are various improved versions of gradient descent algorithms. In object-oriented
language implementations, different gradient descent algorithms are often encapsulated into
objects called optimizers.

⚫

⚫

The purpose of algorithm improvement includes but is not limited to:


Accelerating algorithm convergence



Avoiding getting trapped in local extrema



Simplifying manual setting of hyperparameters, especially the learning rate (LR)

Commonly used optimizers include SGD, Momentum, Nesterov, AdaGrad, RMSprop, and Adam.

51

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Momentum Optimizer
⚫

Imagine a ball that starts from a random point and rolls
down along a surface. The ball rolls faster and faster
due to gravity. The momentum optimizer can accelerate
SGD by adding 𝛾𝑣𝑡−1 and suppress fluctuations.

𝑣𝑡 = 𝛾𝑣𝑡−1 − 𝜂𝛻𝜃 𝐽 𝜃
𝜃 ← 𝜃 + 𝑣𝑡


52

In this formula, 𝑣𝑡−1 is the reverse gradient in the last
update, and 𝛻𝜃 𝐽 𝜃 is the reverse gradient in the current
update. 𝜂 is the learning rate. 0≤𝛾<1 is a constant, and is
referred to as a momentum that indicates the degree to
which an original update direction needs to be retained.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The process of finding an extremum point of the loss function is similar to that of a ball,
which, starting from a random point, rolls down the error surface. The ball has a certain
momentum. In physics, the momentum of an object is equal to the mass of the object times
its velocity. Momentum used in our situation is similar. It helps to maintain the previous
update direction to a certain extent, and also slightly adjusts the direction based on the
gradient of the current batch. For instance, the direction of the previous update is forward,
and the current update, according to the calculated gradient, is going left. This change
seems too radical. Therefore, to make a compromise, let's go left forward. So it seems that
the last update has some momentum. This way, learning can be accelerated while
improving stability, and the network gains certain ability to avoid being trapped in local
minima.

AdaGrad Optimizer
⚫

A common feature between Stochastic Gradient Descent (SGD) and the momentum optimizer
is that each parameter is updated using the same learning rate.

⚫

The idea of AdaGrad is to set different learning rates for different parameters, with the learning

rates varying as the model is being trained.

Large learning rate
53

Small learning rate

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• AdaGrad is one of the earliest adaptive learning rate algorithms. Its main objective is to
accelerate convergence for sparse gradient parameters. The way the AdaGrad optimizer
works is similar to the game of golf. At the very beginning, when you are far away from the
hole, you hit the ball hard. But when you hit the ball the second time, where it is closer to
the hole, you use less force. You can think of the force with which you hit the ball as the
learning rate.

Adam Optimizer
⚫

The Adam Optimizer adjusts the momentum and learning rate for each parameter during
training.

+

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

4. Architecture Design for Neural Networks

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Designing the Network Structure
⚫

Observe the following when designing the structure of an artificial neural network:


The number of neurons at the input layer should match the number of features in the training data.



In terms of a classification problem, the number of neurons at the output layer is typically equal to
the number of classes used for classification.



Generally, a larger quantity of neurons at each hidden layer can lead to higher classification
precision, but it also increases the computational load.



56

Increasing the depth is typically much more efficient than increasing the width.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Does Increasing the Network Depth Always Lead to Higher Model
Precision?
⚫

In deep learning, increasing the network depth typically leads to the following issues:


Increased compute consumption (which can be solved using a GPU cluster)



Overfitting (which can be avoided by using a larger training set and regularization methods such as
Dropout)



Vanishing or exploding gradients (which can be avoided using methods like initialization and batch
normalization)

⚫

Theoretically, a deeper network should have better performance. But in order for it to happen,
you have to first address the network degradation problem.

57

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In a neural network, the depth of the network, that is, how many layers it has, is very
important. It is generally true that as the depth increases, the neural network can extract
more abstract and semantic information. However, it is also found that simply adding more
layers can lead to these problems we list here, but all these problems are solvable.
• Increasing the network depth can only improve model precision to a point. Experiments
show that the degradation problem is not caused by overfitting, because even on the
training set, increasing the network depth can lead to lower precision. The degradation
problem shows that deep neural networks cannot be optimized by simply increasing the
depth.

Batch Normalization
⚫

Batch normalization is a method used to make the training of artificial neural networks faster by normalizing the
inputs of each layer.

⚫

It was published in the 2015 Google paper titled "Batch Normalization: Accelerating Deep Network Training by

Reducing Internal Covariate Shift", and was quickly and widely adopted since then.
𝑥1

𝑊1

𝑧1

𝑧ǁ 1

𝑧Ƹ 1

𝑊1

𝑧2

𝑧ǁ 2

𝑧Ƹ 2

𝑥3

𝑊1

𝑧3

𝑧ǁ 3

𝑧Ƹ 3

𝜇

𝜇 and 𝜎 depends
on 𝑧 𝑖

𝑥

𝑊1

𝑧

𝑧−𝜇
𝜎

𝜇, 𝜎 are from
batch

𝜎

𝛽

𝛾

𝑧Ƹ 𝑖 = 𝛾⨀𝑧ǁ 𝑖 + 𝛽
𝑧ǁ

𝛾, 𝛽 are network
parameters

𝑧Ƹ

Accelerate training through data normalization
58

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Batch normalization standardizes the activation input values of neurons in each neural
network layer to follow a standard normal distribution, with a mean of 0 and a variance of
1. This means that the activation input values fall within the region where the nonlinear
function is most sensitive to the input. In this way, Consequently, small changes in the input
result in significant changes in the loss function, increasing the gradient and preventing the
vanishing gradient problem.
• Advantages of batch normalization:
▫ Batch normalization accelerates model learning by normalizing the inputs of each
layer of the neural network. By means of normalization and linear transformation,
batch normalization enables an average value and a variance of input data for each
layer of network to be within a specific range, so that a next layer of network does
not need to continuously adapt to an input change of a bottom-layer network,
thereby implementing decoupling between layers and allowing independent learning
of each layer. This helps speed up learning of the entire neural network.
▫ Batch normalization makes the model less sensitive to parameters in the network,
reduces complexity of training and parameter tuning of the neural network model,
allows network learning more stable, has a relatively low requirement for
initialization, and uses a large learning rate.
▫ Batch normalization supports more activation functions (such as sigmoid, tanh, and
ReLU) to alleviate the vanishing gradient problem. Gradient decays rapidly as the
sigmoid level increases, making it unsuitable in the deep neural network. The
problem with ReLU is that it can cause neurons to "die" (that is, ReLU falls into the
zero area). Batch normalization can normalize inputs so that these activation
functions can be used.
▫ Batch normalization has a regularization effect to some extent. In batch
normalization, the mean values and variances of mini-batches are used to estimate
the mean value and variance of the overall training samples. Although the data in
each batch is obtained from the overall samples, the mean values and variances of
different mini-batches are different. This adds random noise to the network learning
process, which is similar to the noise brought by dropout disabling neurons to
network training. To a certain extent, the model is regularized.

Residual Connections
⚫

Solution: The primary idea behind residual networks (or ResNet) is mapping multiple layers into a single layer,
turning a deep network into a shallow one, thus mitigating the vanishing gradient problem.

⚫

ResNet introduces the concept of an identity shortcut connection that skips one or more layers, making it possible to
train networks of hundreds or even thousands of layers while achieving superb performance.

X

weight layer
𝐹(𝑋)

relu
weight layer

X
identity

𝐹 𝑋 +X
relu
59

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In ResNet, when the network gets too deep, performance degrades due to the vanishing
gradient problem. The residual structure of ResNet helps mitigate this problem.

extensively used in various functions, including image processing, image recognition,
and image generation. This chapter provides an introduction to the fundamental
theories and practices of image processing, as well as the theories and techniques
involved in image recognition and generation.

Computer Vision Overview
Computer vision is an interdisciplinary field that focuses on enabling computers to perceive and

⚫

understand visual information, similar to how humans do.
While the human visual system perceives the world in three dimensions, computers process images and

⚫

videos, which are typically two-dimensional representations. The goal of computer vision is to develop

algorithms and techniques that allow computers to interpret and analyze visual data captured by
cameras and other sensors.

Human Eye Imaging
⚫

The images that humans see are created through the reflection and absorption of light energy by both the
illumination source and the elements within the scene. An illumination source emits light towards an object, which
then reflects or refracts the light. This light then enters the human eye, allowing the object to be seen.

⚫

We can use the 𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦) function to represent an image. 𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦) consists of two parts: the light source component
𝑖(𝑥, 𝑦) emitted to the observed scene and the light source component 𝑟 𝑥, 𝑦 reflected by the object in the scene.
The size of 𝑖(𝑥, 𝑦) is determined by the illumination source, and that of 𝑟 𝑥, 𝑦 is determined by the characteristics
of the imaged object.

Illumination source

11

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Sensing and Acquisition
⚫

A digital image is captured using a process similar to how the human eye functions. To generate images, an array consisting of
numerous photosensitive sensors is used.

⚫

The image acquisition process involves merging the input electrical energy with a photoreceptive sensor material, converting the
input energy into a voltage, and then sampling and quantizing the resulting voltage wave to obtain a discrete digital image.
The number of sensors, dimensions, and sensing capabilities of the sensors determines the quality of the imaging.

⚫

Digital image acquired after scene elements are processed by the imaging system
12

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Cornea and crystalline lens: lens
• Retina: photosensitive unit

Image Digitization
⚫

Most sensors output continuous voltage waveforms. Image digitization refers to the process of
converting continuous-tone images into digital images that can be processed by computers.

Digital image acquired using a 30 × 30 grayscale sensor
⚫

Image digitization involves two processing steps: sampling and quantization.

13

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Sampling
⚫

When an image is digitized, the sampling process converts it from a spatially continuous image
to discrete points.

⚫

The resolution of a discrete image is determined by its size, which is measured in width and
height. Width refers to the number of details in the horizontal direction, whereas height refers
to the number of details in the vertical direction.

⚫

Example:

14



An image with a resolution of 640 × 480 is made up of 307,200 points.



An image with a resolution of 1920 × 1080 is made up of 2,073,600 points.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Effects of Different Sampling Resolutions
⚫

The smaller the sampling interval, the more sampling points in the image. This results in a high spatial resolution and
better image quality but a larger data volume.

⚫

The following images are displayed with the resolution reduced from 1000 × 1000 to 10 × 10.

Quantization
⚫

Quantization in digital image processing is the process of converting the continuous sensor signals at
sampling points into discrete integer values.

⚫

The grayscale level refers to a range of change for each sampling point of a quantified discrete image. It

is typically an integral power of 2 and is represented by m levels or n bits. The greater the number of
grayscale levels in the image data, the better the visual quality. The most commonly used images on
computers are 8-bit images.
⚫

Example:


An 8-bit image indicates that each sampling point has 256 (2 8) levels.



There are 256 levels discernible from the darkest to the brightest level.



In a 32-level grayscale image, each sampling point has 32 levels discernible from the darkest to the brightest
level.

16

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Quantization converts samples with a continuous range of values into discrete values.

Quantization Effects of Different Grayscale Levels
⚫

The more the quantization levels, the more the image levels. This results in a high grayscale resolution
and good image quality but a larger data volume.

⚫

The following figures show how an image changes when the grayscale level is reduced from 256 to 2.

17

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Pixel
⚫

Each sampling point in a digital image is referred to as a pixel. A pixel's position can be described by its
coordinates (𝑥, 𝑦) in an image, and its grayscale value ranges from 0 to 255.

⚫

For a digital image with the resolution of M × N, the pixel in the upper left corner is usually recorded as

the origin (0,0). The horizontal coordinate range is [0, 𝑀 − 1], and the vertical coordinate range is
[0, 𝑁 − 1].
⚫

The data dimension of a pixel is called a channel.

(4,1)

(3,4)

(x,y)

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Storage of Digital Images
⚫

The grayscale images described previously have only one channel that records the brightness of each pixel. For
instance, for an 8-bit image, 0 represents the darkest shade (black), and 255 represents the brightest shade (white).

21

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Computers process numbers. To enable a computer to understand an image, we must
convert the image into numbers.
• An image is composed of numerous pixels. A pixel refers to a small square in an image. Each
square has a specific position and an allocated color value. The colors and positions of the
squares determine the appearance of the image. A pixel can be considered as an indivisible
unit or element of an image. A pixel cannot be divided into smaller units or elements, and it
has only one color.
• As shown in the figure, for a computer, a black-and-white image is a huge matrix of
numbers. Each number is an integer from 0 to 255. The value 0 indicates black, and 255
indicates white.

Color Image – RGB
⚫

To represent color images, multi-channel digital images are typically used, with the most
common method being the RGB color space. In this color space, each pixel consists of three
dimensions, representing the intensity levels of the red (R), green (G), and blue (B) components.

⚫

Examples:


(255,0,0) indicates pure red.



(124,252,0) indicates lawn green.



(135,206,235) indicates sky blue.

Width

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Color Image – HSV
⚫

Another widely used color space is the Hue, Saturation, Value (HSV) color space, which can be
represented as a cone. Hue (H) is measured in degrees and ranges from 0 to 360. Saturation (S)
represents the ratio of a color's purity to the maximum purity, ranging from 0 to 1. Value (V)

signifies the brightness of the color, also ranging from 0 to 1.
⚫

The color spaces similar to HSV are as follows:


HSL (L: lightness)



HIS (I: intensity)

Other Color Spaces
⚫

YUV
The YUV color space consists of the luminance signal Y and two color difference signals R-Y and B-Y. The luminance signal Y and



chrominance signals U and V of the YUV color space are separated. A YUV value that only contains the Y signal component may
indicate a black-and-white grayscale image. The YUV color space is typically used for image compression and transmission.
⚫

CMYK
The CMYK color space is used in printing, and CMYK refers to the four inks used in some color printing: cyan (C), magenta (M),



yellow (Y), and black (K). Overprinting of the four colors with different dot area ratios produces rich colors and tones.
⚫

Lab


24

The LAB color space is larger than the RGB and CMYK color spaces. Any color in nature can be represented using LAB.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• YUV: Human eyes are more sensitive to highlighted information. That is, UV data can be
compressed so that it cannot be detected by human eyes easily. The first step of a
compression algorithm is to convert RGB data into YUV data. UV is compressed more than Y
to balance the image effect and compression ratio.

Color Space Conversion
⚫

In computer vision, especially in the design of algorithms related to color recognition, various color
spaces are often used together. Widely used color spaces such as RGB, HSV, and YUV can be converted
by using formulas, and this process is referred to as color space conversion. The formula for calculating

the color space conversion is complex. Typically, the image processing library provides color space
conversion APIs for users to invoke.

Grayscale Conversion
⚫

To facilitate calculation, a multi-channel color image is often converted into a single-channel grayscale image in
scenarios where colors are not relevant. This process is called grayscale image conversion. For BGR images, the
common grayscale image conversion methods are as follows:

⚫



Maximum value method: 𝐼 = max(𝑅, 𝐺, 𝐵)



Mean value method: 𝐼 = (𝑅 + 𝐺 + 𝐵)/3



Weighted mean value method: 𝐼 = 0.11 ∗ 𝐵 + 0.59 ∗ 𝐺 + 0.30 ∗ 𝑅

Grayscale image conversion can also be performed by directly invoking the APIs of the image processing library.

26

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Weighted mean value: Human eyes are most sensitive to green, followed by red and blue.

Connected Region
⚫

In an image, if any two pixels in a pixel set are connected and they are not connected to pixels outside the set, the pixel set is called

⚫

In traditional image processing algorithms, image preprocessing involves removing irrelevant information from images, restoring
useful real information, enhancing the detectability of relevant information, and simplifying the data. This process improves the

reliability of feature extraction, image segmentation, matching, and recognition.
⚫

Image preprocessing involves grayscale transformation, geometric correction, image enhancement, and image filtering.

32

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Image preprocessing processes input images and outputs processed images.
• Image preprocessing is necessary for both conventional image processing and deep
learning-based image processing. In traditional image processing algorithms, image
preprocessing involves removing irrelevant information from images, restoring useful real
information, enhancing the detectability of relevant information, and simplifying the data.
This process improves the reliability of feature extraction, image segmentation, matching,
and recognition.
• Deep learning does not require feature extraction, but requires image preprocessing. The
reason will be given at the end of this section.

Grayscale Transformation
⚫

Grayscale transformation involves transforming the grayscale value of each point in an image into another grayscale
value based on a specified mapping function. This transformation is performed independently on a pixel. The
original pixel value is 𝑠, the mapping function used for the transformation is 𝑇(s), and the pixel value obtained after
the transformation is 𝑑.
𝑑 = 𝑇(𝑠)

⚫

Various grayscale transformation functions can be used to enhance the visual effect of images. For an image with a
grayscale level of 𝐿, the mapping function maps an input value in the [0, 𝐿 − 1] range to an output value in the [0, 𝐿 −
1] range. The graph of the mapping function can be generated to indicate the effect of grayscale transformation.

⚫

Grayscale transformation is performed to produce clearer images, and provides the following capabilities:

Contrast broadening





Histogram equalization

Image Contrast
⚫

Contrast is the color difference between adjacent pixels. Typically, it indicates the clarity of an
image. The higher the contrast, the greater the differences between colors. If the contrast of an
image is too high, the image appears very glaring. The lower the contrast, the smaller the

differences between colors.
⚫

Formula for calculating the contrast:
𝐶 = ෍ 𝛿 𝑖, 𝑗 2 𝑃𝛿 (𝑖, 𝑗)
𝛿

⚫

𝛿 𝑖, 𝑗 represents the grayscale differences between adjacent pixels. 𝑃𝛿 (𝑖, 𝑗) is the pixel
distribution probability of the adjacent pixels whose grayscale difference is 𝛿.

35

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Contrast Stretching
⚫

If an image is underexposed or overexposed, its grayscale range is limited to a narrow range, and the image appears
blurry and lacks detail. Applying linear contrast stretching can linearly expand the grayscale values of each pixel,
significantly improving the image quality.

⚫

Contrast stretching operates in a point-to-point manner, enhancing the significant portions of an image while
suppressing less important areas without altering the overall dynamic range of the pixel values.

Dynamic Range Adjustment
⚫

A dynamic range refers to the range of light brightness in an image scene.

⚫

Impact of the dynamic range on human vision: Human eyes can detect only a limited range of
grayscale changes. If the dynamic range is too large, a great brightness value masks all signals in
the dark area.

⚫

Dynamic range adjustment rule: The dynamic range is reduced to enlarge the change range of
the desired area, thereby improving the image quality.

44

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Generally, the logarithmic method is used for dynamic range adjustment, as human eyes
process signals in a similar way as logarithmic operators.

Histogram
⚫

A histogram reflects the frequencies of pixels with different grayscale levels in an image. It is a
graph showing the relationship between the frequency and grayscale level. It uses the grayscale
level as the x-axis and the frequency as the y-axis. It is an important feature of images and

reflects the grayscale distribution of images.
⚫

Histogram-based image transformation is a method based on the probability theory. By
changing the histogram of an image and changing the grayscale value of each pixel in the
image, you can enhance the visual effect of the image.

⚫

While grayscale transformation focuses on single pixels of an image, histogram-based
transformation considers the grayscale value distribution of the entire image.

47

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Histogram Equalization
⚫

Histogram equalization adjusts an image's histogram, that is, the grayscale probability distribution graph, to make
grayscale levels of the image equalized and effectively enhance the overall contrast of the image.

⚫

Histogram equalization automatically calculates the transformation function and generates the output image with

an equalized histogram. This feature effectively improves the image quality by resolving over darkness, over
brightness, and unclear details.
⚫

Basic rule: Grayscale levels with more pixels in an image are stretched and those with fewer pixels are reduced. In
this way, all grayscale levels are fully utilized to generate a clear image.

⚫

APIs in common image processing libraries can be called to perform histogram operations.

51

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Histogram Equalization Effect

55

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The result obtained from the preceding HE algorithm has some problems: In areas where
grayscale levels are concentrated, the histogram becomes quite sparse. As a result, the
contrast is too large and becomes noise. Some areas become darker or brighter after
adjustment, but details are lost.
• HE: global equalization -> CLHE: limited contrast -> AHE: partial equalization but unsmooth
transition -> CLAHE: weakening partial noise amplification and ensuring smooth transition
through interpolation

Histogram Specification (1)
⚫

Histogram equalization always generates an output image that is globally equalized. In practical applications,
however, it is often necessary to enhance specific grayscale ranges, such as dark areas or bright areas. Histogram
specification can be used to adjust the histogram distribution on demand. This customized adjustment is a
characteristic of histogram specification.

⚫

The histogram specification also adjusts the histogram of the original image so that its probability distribution
approximates the probability distribution of the target histogram.

⚫

To use histogram specification, calculate the most suitable target histogram based on experience and knowledge.
The target histogram and original image are used as the input to generate an image with the specified histogram and
enhanced effect.

56

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Histogram Specification (2)

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Filtering
⚫

Different from the preceding two methods, image filtering is a local processing method. The output value of pixel 𝑃
is determined by the pixel values of 𝑃 and its neighborhood 𝑁 in the input image. Image filtering can be calculated
using the following formula:

𝑂 𝑖, 𝑗 = ෍ 𝐼(𝑖 + 𝑚, 𝑗 + 𝑛) ∙ 𝐾(𝑚, 𝑛)
𝑚,𝑛
⚫

The calculation method is to perform a template operation on the pixel value of neighborhood 𝑁 and a subimage
with the same size as the neighborhood. The subimage is referred to as a template, kernel, or filter.

⚫

Common template operations include template convolution and template sorting.

Grayscale transformation is point-based processing,
and its output value is related to a specified pixel.

Filtering (subgraph)

Histogram transformation is global processing, and its
output value is related to the entire image.

58

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In image processing, filtering removes a specific band frequency from a signal, thus
preserving the required band frequency. This has the following benefits:
▫ Eliminating noises from images through low-pass filtering. The noises in images are
generally high-frequency signals.
▫ Extracting image features for image recognition: The features are generally edge
texture features, which correspond to high-pass filtering. The edges and texture
details in images are high-frequency signals.

Image Filter Types
⚫

⚫

Smoothing spatial filter: removes unimportant details from images to reduce noise.


Mean filter



Median filter



Maximum and minimum filter

Sharpening spatial filter: highlights blurred details in images.

59



First-order differential filter: gradient operator



Second-order differential filter: Laplace operator

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Smoothing filters mainly use the mean (or median) value of the neighborhood to replace
the central pixel in the template, thereby weakening the differences from the
neighborhood to smooth the image and reduce noise. On the contrary, sharpening filters
use the differentiation of the neighborhood as an operator to increase the pixel differences
between the neighborhood and highlight the abrupt changes in images.

Mean Filtering
⚫

The mean filter is a filter for which all template weights are 1. The average value of the neighborhoods of
a pixel is used as the output result. Mean filtering can be used to smooth images and eliminate noise.
However, as the size of the template increases, images become more blurred. Mean filtering is often

used for image blurring.

1

1

1

1

1

1

1

1
Original

60

3 × 3 mean filtering

5 × 5 mean filtering

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• As the original image is large, the 3 × 3 mean filtering may not have an obvious effect.

Median Filtering
⚫

The median filter is a filter of the template sorting operation. It replaces the original pixel value with the median
output of the pixel values sorted in the neighborhood. It reduces noise while retaining the sharpness of the original
image. It does not change the grayscale value of the original image.

⚫

Median filtering is commonly used. A median filter can effectively reduce random salt and pepper noise while
effectively protecting edge information of images. However, median filtering causes non-linear changes, which may
damage the linear relationship of pixels. Therefore, it is not applicable to images with many details such as points
and lines or high-precision images.

Original
61

3 × 3 mean filtering

3 × 3 median filtering

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Salt and pepper noise refers to the random white and black dots that appear on images.
They may be generated by image sensors, transmission channels, or decoding. Salt noise
has a high grayscale level, and pepper noise has a low grayscale level. Generally, they
appear at the same time.

Maximum and Minimum Filtering
⚫

Maximum and minimum filtering is a conservative image processing method. Similar to median filtering, this method first sorts the
values of surrounding pixels and central pixel, and then compares the central pixel value with the minimum and maximum pixel
values. If the central pixel value is less than the minimum pixel value or greater than the maximum pixel value, the central pixel
value is replaced with the minimum pixel value or maximum pixel value.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Properties of Image Differentiation (1)
⚫

⚫

First-order differentiation:


In a constant grayscale area, the differential value of the image is 0.



The differential value at the start point of the grayscale step or slope is not 0.



The differential value along the slope is not 0.

Second-order differentiation:

63



In a constant area, the second-order differential value is 0.



The differential value at the start point of the grayscale step or slope is not 0.



The differential value along the slope is 0.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The grayscale value is not transformed, and the natural differential value is 0.
• A step indicates that the grayscale value changes sharply, while a slope indicates that the
grayscale value changes slowly. If the grayscale value changes, the differential value is not
0.
• From the properties of the first-order and second-order differentiation, it can be learned
that if the grayscale value changes, neither the first-order differential value nor the secondorder differential value is 0, and that if the grayscale value is constant, the two differential
values are both 0. In other words, the changes in the image grayscale values can be
obtained using either first-order differentiation or second-order differentiation.

Properties of Image Differentiation (2)
⚫

Generally, a slope is formed for the edges of an image.

⚫

If the first-order differential value is not 0 at the slope, the edge obtained using first-order
differentiation is coarse. If the second-order differential value is 0 at the slope, but the values at
both ends of the slope are not 0, and the symbols of the values are different, the second-order
differentiation obtains double edges of a pixel width separated by 0.

⚫

Compared with first-order differentiation, second-order differentiation enhances image details
better and features easier computation.

64

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In image processing, the gradient means the change speed of the pixel grayscale value. In
digital image processing, due to the particularity of the pixel property, the calculus is used
to calculate the difference of the current pixel in the partial differential direction. The
calculation does not involve derivation, and only requires simple addition and subtraction
operations.
• For the gradient of discrete images, the first-order partial derivatives are approximately
represented by the first-order differences, that is:
▫ 𝑓𝑥 ′ = 𝑓 𝑥 + 1, 𝑦 – 𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦)
▫ 𝑓𝑦 ′ = 𝑓 𝑥, 𝑦 + 1 – 𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦)
• Similarly, second-order differences are as follows:
▫ 𝑓𝑥 ′′ = 𝑓 𝑥 – 1, 𝑦 + 𝑓 𝑥 + 1, 𝑦 – 2𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦)
▫ 𝑓𝑦 ′′ = 𝑓 𝑥, 𝑦 – 1 + 𝑓 𝑥, 𝑦 + 1 – 2𝑓(𝑥, 𝑦)
• Compared with the Prewitt operator, the Sobel operator involves weight. The impact of the
distance between adjacent pixels on the current pixel may vary. A closer pixel has greater
impact on the current pixel. In this way, the image is sharpened and the edge outline is
highlighted.
• Laplacian operator: The first kernel supports four domains. The second kernel supports
eight domains.

equal to 1, the effect is as follows.

Canny Edge Detection Algorithm
⚫

The Canny edge detection algorithm is composed of five steps:

68



Use a Gaussian filter to smooth the image and reduce noise.



Calculate the gradient intensity and direction of each pixel in an image.



Use non-maximum suppression to eliminate the spurious response caused by edge detection.



Use double-threshold detection to determine real and potential edges.



Suppress isolated weak edges to complete edge detection.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Geometric Transformation of Images
⚫

Geometric transformation of images describes the position, size, and shape changes of images
through mathematical modeling.

⚫

Geometric transformation of an image does not change the values of pixels, but changes their
positions.

⚫

The following types of geometric transformation are available:


Affine transformation: representation of geometric transformation using mathematical mapping
transformation formulas

69



Shape transformation: image zoom-in, zoom-out, and cropping



Position transformation: image translation, reflection, and rotation

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Affine Transformation (1)
⚫

Affine transformation is a method for performing linear coordinate transformation on an image in a twodimensional plane, that is, performing linear transformation and translation on the image, such as image translation,
scaling, rotation, and reflection. Affine transformation retains "parallelism" and "flatness" of an image, that is, a
straight line and a parallel line remain unchanged after affine transformation.

⚫

Homogeneous coordinates were introduced to represent geometric transformation in the form of the coordinate
vector multiplied by the transformation matrix, especially to adapt to translation.

⚫

In essence, a coordinate is added to solve the problem. Based on homogeneous coordinates, affine transformation is
defined as follows:

𝑥 ′ = 𝑎𝑥 + 𝑏𝑦 + ∆𝑥
𝑦 ′ = 𝑐𝑥 + 𝑑𝑦 + ∆𝑦

70

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In the Cartesian coordinate system, vector (x, y) is a point on the z=0 plane, and vector (x, y,
1) is a point on the z=1 contour plane.
• It makes no substantial difference to graphs, but facilitates subsequent matrix operations.

Affine Transformation (2)
⚫

The affine transformation formula is as follows:

of perspective transformation has eight unknown numbers. Four groups of mapping points
are needed to determine a three-dimensional space and solve the equation.

Interpolation
⚫

The values of 𝑥, 𝑦 in a digital image are integers, but the coordinates (𝑥′, 𝑦′) obtained after
coordinate transformation may not be integers. The pixel values at non-integer coordinates
need to be calculated using the pixel values of neighboring integer coordinates. This process is

called interpolation.
⚫

There are many calculation methods of interpolation, and the simplest one is nearest neighbor
interpolation. It uses the grayscale value at the nearest integer coordinates of point (𝑥′, 𝑦′) as
the value of point (𝑥′, 𝑦′).

⚫

Nearest neighbor interpolation features simple calculation, but it is less accurate and may
destroy the linear relationship in the image. To improve accuracy, you can use bilinear
interpolation.
75

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Bilinear Interpolation
⚫

Bilinear interpolation uses the four nearest adjacent pixel values of point (𝑥′, 𝑦′)
to perform interpolation calculation. For example, the four pixel values are
𝑖, 𝑗 , 𝑖 + 1, 𝑗 , 𝑖, 𝑗 + 1 , and 𝑖 + 1, 𝑗 + 1 .

Rotation (2)
⚫

If the rotation axis is not located at the origin, the calculation of the transformation matrix is complex. The operation

through translation.

Color Image Processing – Hue Enhancement
⚫

The human eyes' perception of the three components of the HSV color space is independent. Therefore, independent component
graphs of the HSV can be processed to enhance the image.

⚫

The image hue can be enhanced by processing the H component of the HSV color space.


Hue adjustment usually adds a small offset to the original value of H so that it has a small angle adjustment in the color circle. After the

adjustment, the hue of the image changes to cool or warm.


82

The value of hue H is measured in degrees and circulates in the color circle. Therefore, hue correction may cause color distortion.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Color Image Processing – Saturation Enhancement
⚫

The image saturation can be enhanced by processing the S component of the HSV color space. Usually the
adjustment of saturation is to multiply the original value of S by a correction coefficient.

83



If the correction coefficient is greater than 1, the saturation is increased and the color of the image looks more vibrant.



If the correction coefficient is less than 1, the saturation is reduced and the image looks less vivid.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Color Image Processing – Brightness Enhancement
⚫

The image brightness can be enhanced by processing the V component of the HSV color space.

⚫

By directly graying a color image, you can obtain a grayscale image representing the image brightness. This process
requires less computation than the HSV color space transformation. However, by enhancing the brightness in the

HSV space, you can obtain an enhanced color image.

84

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Application of Image Preprocessing in Deep Learning

Preprocessing is unnecessary for image processing algorithms in deep learning, but image
preprocessing technology is utilized for data augmentation in training datasets.

To enhance image processing tasks, techniques such as adding random noise to data, increasing
dataset samples, and improving data sample space complexity are employed.

Image data augmentation commonly involves scaling, stretching, adding noise, flipping,
rotation, translation, shearing, contrast adjustment, and channel transformation.

85

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Content: The properties of objects in images and the relationships between

Three levels of image processing

Characteristics: The input is an image feature, and the output is image content.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• If computer vision is considered as a one-way process, it can be divided into three levels:
the low level, medium level, and high level.
▫ Low level: This involves pixel processing, such as brightness enhancement,
histograms, and histogram equalization. It is called image processing.
▫ Medium level: Features like edges, orientations, and textures are analyzed to
segment images. It is called image analysis.
▫ High level: This aims to extract semantic information, such as identifying a tiger in the
middle of an image, a beach below the tiger, and a green grassland, representing a
wilderness scene. It is called image understanding.

Image Processing Task – Image Classification
⚫

Image classification is one of the basic research topics of image processing in the AI field and a focus of
computer vision.

⚫

Image classification determines the category to which an input image belongs in the fixed K categories

based on the image processing technology. The size of K depends on the dataset.

• Input and output:
▫ Input: image
▫ Output: category (represented by the probability value)

Papaver rhoeas

Image Processing Task – Object Detection
⚫

Object detection is a classic image processing and computer vision technology in AI. It is used in a wide range of
scenarios, such as traffic surveillance, image retrieval, object recognition, and human-computer interaction. Object
detection identifies the objects that people are interested in from images. The objects can be processed using
intelligent algorithms.

car

car
car

car

car
car
car
car

car

90

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Due to the varying appearances, shapes, and postures of diverse objects, along with the
interference of factors like illumination and obstruction during imaging, object detection is
always the most challenging task in computer vision.
• Object recognition is slightly different from object detection, though they use similar
techniques. Object recognition finds out the instance of an object in an image. This process
is not classification. Instead, it determines whether the object appears in the image and
locates the object if it appears.

Image Processing Task – Image Segmentation
⚫

Image segmentation partitions an image into multiple image segments, also known as image regions.

⚫

It has a range of algorithms and use cases. Common image segmentation methods include connected
domain segmentation, motion segmentation, and object segmentation.

91

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Object segmentation: semantic segmentation and instance segmentation
▫ Semantic segmentation refers to pixel-level image recognition, that is, categorizing
each pixel in an image into a class and assigning a label to each pixel.
▫ Instance segmentation identifies the instances of every object in an image and
assigns a label to each pixel of every instance.
• Segmentation is a pixel-level description of an image, and defines each pixel class
(instance). It is applicable to scenarios with a relatively high understanding requirement, for
example, segmentation of road and non-road in autonomous driving.

• Input and output:
▫ Input: image
▫ Output: segmented images with the same resolution as the input image and with
labels of each pixel class

Image Processing Task – Object Tracking
⚫

Object tracking is a fundamental research area in computer vision with extensive applications such as intelligent
transportation, security surveillance, human-machine interaction, and autonomous driving.

⚫

Tracking algorithms can be used to obtain the time-based trajectories of objects and analyze the moving behavior of

the objects.

92

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Processing Task – Optical Character Recognition
⚫

Optical Character Recognition (OCR) identifies the text in images or scanned documents using image
processing techniques such as character object detection and object classification. It improves efficiency
as manual input is not required. It can recognize characters on ID cards, driver's licenses, vehicle licenses,

receipts, customs documents, and general tables and text.

93

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Processing Task – Content Detection
⚫

Content detection is a technology that uses computers to process, analyze, and understand images to
identify objects in different modes.

⚫

Image content detection can intelligently and precisely understand image content and make intelligent

album management, picture retrieval and classification, and scenario- or object-based advertising more
intuitive.

Image Processing Task – Image Generation
⚫

Image generation generates an image from another with some areas modified, or generates a new image.


Super resolution increases the resolution of images and predicts image features at different magnifications.



Style migration applies the style of a domain or a few images to other domains or images, for example, applying an abstract style to a realistic
image.



Image inpainting repairs missing parts in images. For example, It can be used to repair old, damaged black-and-white photos and videos.

Traditional Image Processing Algorithms
⚫

The emergence of deep learning is a technological revolution in image processing. Traditional image processing
algorithms lag far behind deep learning.

⚫

However, deep learning relies heavily on robust compute and a massive number of datasets. When these conditions

cannot be met, traditional image processing algorithms can still meet requirements in some scenarios.
⚫

Many supplementary programs use traditional algorithms to complete processing of tasks started using deep
learning. Learning traditional image processing algorithms gives you a better understanding of image technologies. It
can help acquire the theoretical understanding needed to optimize and innovate deep learning techniques.

Image

Image preprocessing

Feature extraction

Traditional image processing method
