Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image analysis and
understanding

Image Feature Extraction
⚫

Digital images are a form of unstructured data, so pattern recognition algorithms are not suitable for processing. If
an image is forcibly expanded into two-dimensional structured data based on pixel grayscale values, a color image
with a resolution of 800 × 600 has a data length of 1,440,000 (800 × 600 × 3) dimensions. Calculating such data is
very complex and inefficient.

⚫

To effectively transform digital images into structured data, feature extraction technology is used to reduce the
dimensionality of data. The main methods are as follows:
Downsampling: reduces the resolution of the image to be analyzed through downsampling
techniques such as scaling.
Region of interest (ROI) segmentation: extracts a desired region from an image through
segmentation to reduce the amount of data to be processed.
Feature descriptor: uses a feature descriptor to transform an image into a fixed-length feature
vector.

98

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Binarization
⚫

Image binarization is a process where the grayscale values of all pixels on an image are set to
either black (0) or white (255). In this way, the entire image is segmented into obvious black
and white areas. (An 8-bit image is used as an example in this section.)

⚫

The most common form of image binarization is thresholding, which sets the colors of pixels
whose grayscale values are greater than a threshold to white (or black), and those whose
grayscale values are less than the threshold to black (or white). This threshold is usually
represented by T.

99

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Binary images play an important role in digital image processing. It can be used for the
extraction of connected regions, morphological processing, and segmentation of regions of
interest.
• Binarization significantly reduces the amount of data in an image and highlights the object
contour. The set property of a binarized image is related only to the position of the point
whose pixel value is 0 or 255, and not to multiple levels of pixel values. This simplifies
processing and reduces the amount of data to be processed in the calculation process.

Adaptive Thresholding
⚫

Since the threshold selected directly affects how the image is binarized, how that threshold is selected a core function of the
binarization algorithm. On way to automatically select a threshold is adaptive thresholding. Adaptive thresholding can be used to
identify an appropriate threshold based on the grayscale distribution of an image.

⚫

The most common types of adaptive thresholding are double peak and OTSU.

Double peak
100

OTSU

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• To adapt to images with uneven illumination, local adaptive thresholding derives from the
adaptive thresholding algorithm. This algorithm calculates a threshold suitable for each
region of an image to achieve the optimal segmentation effect.
• To address a specific issue, choosing or designing an appropriate adaptive thresholding
algorithm can greatly improve the segmentation result and facilitate subsequent
processing.
• Double peak method
▫ The double peak method is an easy-to-understand adaptive thresholding algorithm. If
the grayscale histogram of an image is obviously bimodal, the grayscale value of the
bottom of the valley between the double peaks is used as the threshold for
segmentation. If the grayscale histogram of an image is flat or has multiple peaks, the
threshold cannot be obtained using the double peak method.
• OTSU
▫ The OTSU algorithm divides an image into the foreground and background based on
the grayscale feature of the image. The larger the inter-class variance between the
foreground and background, the greater the differences between the two parts of
the image. If an inappropriate threshold is used, the inter-class variance between the
foreground and background becomes smaller. Therefore, all possible thresholds are
traversed, and the threshold that maximizes the inter-class variance is used as the
optimal threshold.

Morphological Processing
⚫

Morphological image processing simplifies image data, enhances shape features, and removes
noise. The basic operations of morphological processing include dilation and erosion. These
operations can be combined to achieve practical algorithms such as opening and closing

operations.
⚫

Morphological processing is often used for noise removal, boundary extraction, object locating,
and region filling.

⚫

Morphological processing can be performed on binary or grayscale images. This section uses

binary images as an example, and the operations also apply to grayscale images.

101

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Basic Morphological Operations – Dilation
⚫

The image to be processed is marked A, and the structure element is marked B. The dilation expands the foreground
area in A based on the shape of B.

⚫

After the dilation, the edge of the foreground area expands into the background area.

⚫

⚫

The image to be processed is marked A, and the structure element is marked B. The erosion shrinks the foreground
area in A according to the shape of B.

⚫

After the erosion operation, the edge of the foreground area is compressed and eroded by the background area.

⚫

Opening
⚫

Opening involves eroding image A with structure element B and then expanding the result with B.

⚫

Opening can filter out bright spots and spurs smaller than the structure element, and it can remove
slender connections. For example, it separates regions that are connected by noise.

Closing
⚫

Closing involves expanding image A with structure element B and then eroding the result with B.

⚫

Closing can fill in dark spots or holes that are smaller than the structure element. It can also connect
small fractured regions and smooth the boundaries. For example, it can merge and connect regions that

are broken due to poor image quality.

external gradient of the image.



Inner boundary: the difference image obtained by subtracting the eroded image from the original image. It is called the
internal gradient of the image.



Morphological gradient: difference between the dilation and the erosion of an image

Feature Descriptor
⚫

In image processing, a feature descriptor is used to convert an image into a feature vector of a
fixed length. Different feature descriptors describe various types of image attributes. Common
feature descriptors used in image recognition include HOG features, LBP features, and Haar

features.
HOG and LBP features are generally used together
with an SVM algorithm for pattern recognition, such
as pedestrian detection and vehicle detection.
Haar features and the AdaBoost algorithm are used
together to deliver good object detection
performance.

107

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Factors to be considered: calculation speed, rotational invariance, scale invariance,
brightness changes, and processing blur
• Ideal feature descriptors: In images with varied sizes, directions, and brightness, the same
feature point should have sufficient similar descriptors, which is known as descriptor
reproducibility.

Image Gradient (1)
⚫

Object contours and edges are significant image features. It is indistinct object contours and subtle changes in pixel and grayscale
values that make an image blurry.

⚫

The gradient direction is the direction in which the function changes most quickly. In an image, the gradient value at an object's
edge is relatively large. Conversely, in smoother parts of the image, the grayscale values change less, resulting in smaller gradients.

In image processing, the gradient magnitude is just called the gradient, and an image composed of gradients is called a gradient
image.

[−1,0,1]

[−1,0,1] 𝑇

108

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Image Gradient (2)
⚫

An image's gradient reflects its edge and contour features, and the gradient is influenced by the
light.

109

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Solution:
▫ Normalization: The gradient of an image is sensitive to the light of the entire image. If
you divide all pixels by 2, the gradient amplitude is also halved.
▫ Block segmentation: The grayscale in the light area is significantly different from that
in the shadow area.

Solution: HOG
⚫

Policies for preventing the interference of light and utilizing the image gradient properly:


Divide an image into several blocks.



Use statistical methods to calculate the pixel gradient histogram in each block to prevent the
interference of light.

⚫

A histogram of oriented gradients (HOG) is a feature descriptor used for object detection in
computer vision and image processing. It constructs features by calculating and collecting
statistics on the HOG of some areas in images.

⚫

HOG features are used together with SVM classifiers widely and successfully in image
recognition, particularly in pedestrian detection.

110

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• First, the image is divided into many small connected regions, which are called cell units.
Then, the gradient and edge direction of each pixel in the cell units are collected to
generate a one-dimensional gradient direction histogram in each cell unit.
• Contrast normalization needs to be performed on histograms in a larger scope (range or
block) of the image to achieve better invariance to illumination and shadow. First, the
density of each histogram in the range is calculated. Then, the cell units in the range are
normalized based on the density. The normalized block descriptor is the HOG descriptor.

Pedestrian Detection: HOG + SVM
⚫

Before the widespread use of deep learning technologies, pedestrian detection algorithms used HOG features and SVM classifiers.

⚫

HOG is a common feature descriptor. It transforms images into vectors that can represent image features and can be used to train
classification models.
Descriptor
HOG/SIFT/SURF
Class "Person"

(𝑥0 , 𝑥1 , … , 𝑥𝑛 )
SVM

(𝑥0 , 𝑥1 , … , 𝑥𝑛 )
Class "No Person"

112

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The HOG feature is operated on local square grids of images, so it has good adaptability to
image angles and light distortion. Subtle body movements of pedestrians do not affect the
detection effect as long as the pedestrians are generally upright. The HOG feature is
suitable for pedestrian detection. However, the HOG feature does not support rotation
invariance and multi-scale detection.
• Room for improvement in HOG:
▫ Color images should be used during image preprocessing. The gradient with the
largest gradient magnitude in the pixel color channel is used as the gradient of the
pixel.
▫ During the preprocessing of grayscale images, the Gaussian function is used to
smooth the images to remove noise.
▫ There are generally three types of HOG structures: rectangular HOG (R-HOG), circular
HOG (C-HOG), and center-surrounded HOG. They are all measured in blocks.
According to the Dalal test result, R-HOG and C-HOG show almost the same detection
performance, and they both outperform center-surrounded HOG.

Support Vector Machines
⚫

Support Vector Machines (SVMs) are a set of supervised learning methods used for
classification and regression.

113

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• SVMs are general linear classifiers that can minimize empirical errors while maximizing
intervals. Therefore, SVMs are also called maximum interval classifiers.
• SVMs used to be the most important models in deep leaning for many years. Until today,
despite the growing influence of neural networks in deep learning, SVMs still show as good
performance and robustness as neural networks on small- and medium-sized datasets.

Local Binary Pattern
⚫

Local binary patterns (LBPs) are descriptors that describe local texture features of images. LBPs have notable advantages like rotation invariance and
grayscale invariance.

⚫

In a 3 × 3 window, the central pixel serves as the threshold, and the threshold is compared with the grayscale values of the eight adjacent pixels. If
the grayscale values of the adjacent pixels are greater than the central pixel value, the position of the pixel is marked as 1. Otherwise, the position of
the pixel is marked as 0. In this way, the comparison can generate an 8-bit binary number, and the LBP value of the central pixel of the window can be
obtained. The LBP value reflects the texture information of the region.

⚫

LBPs can show the local texture information of images well. They have been continuously improved and optimized and variants such as circular LBPs
and rotation LBPs have emerged.

114

19

1

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• LBPs are operators used to describe local features (textures) of images. They are easy to
use and show good performance. They are widely used in many fields of computer vision,
including object recognition, object detection, lip recognition, expression detection, and
dynamic texture.
• The LBP value of the central pixel reflects the texture information of the surrounding areas
of the pixel: grayscale invariance.
• Rotation invariance: The 8-bit binary number rotates clockwise from the pixel in the upper
left corner. The LBP features in the circular neighborhoods are continuously rotated to
generate a series of LBP feature values. Among them, the minimum LBP feature value is
used as the LBP feature of the central pixel.

Haar Features
⚫

Haar features reflect the grayscale changes of images. There are four types of Haar features: edge features, linear features, central
features, and diagonal features. Black and white rectangular boxes are combined into a feature template. Within the feature
template, the weight values are multiplied by the sum of black rectangular pixels, with the weight values multiplied by the sum of
white rectangular pixels subtracted. The result is the Haar feature value of the image in the area where the template is located.

⚫

Haar features use different feature matrices to extract edge features, linear features, central features, and diagonal features.
Through the adjustment of the size and position of the feature template, numerous features can be exhaustively listed in the image
window. The following figure shows the structures of some common Haar features.

When the white areas are larger than the black areas, a
larger weight is usually used to calculate the pixel sum of
the black areas. For example, the weight for black areas is 2,
and that for white areas is 1.

Process of Extracting Haar Features
⚫

To extract the Haar features from an image, perform the following four steps:

119

1.

2.

3.

Use other different Haar feature matrices to scan the image.

4.

Concatenate all features into a feature vector.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Advantages:
▫ The calculation workload is small, with only addition and subtraction operations. The
features can be extracted quickly.
▫ The Haar features have translation invariance.
▫ The Haar-like features have scale invariance because matrices of different sizes are
used.
▫ The Haar features have rotation invariance because matrices of different angles are
used.

• Restrictions:
▫ If the matrices are large, the calculation workload is also heavy.
▫ The Haar features do not have illumination invariance.

AdaBoost
⚫

Adaptive boosting (AdaBoost) is a landmark algorithm because it is the first algorithm that can
adapt to the training error rates of weak learners.

⚫

AdaBoost works as follows:


First, the same initial weight is assigned to each sample. After each round of learner training, the
weight of each sample is adjusted based on the performance of the learner. The weight of invalid
samples is increased so that more attention can be paid to them. The results obtained through
repeated training are weighted and combined.

121

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Section "AdaBoost" in Machine Learning Methods, written by Lihang

⚫

People perceive images through local features.

Image Processing Using a Fully-connected Network
⚫

When an image is input to a fully connected network, the image is expanded into a vector,
resulting in the loss of the spatial relationships between pixels in the image. Processing images
using a fully-connected network has the following disadvantages:


Humans understand images through local features, but each neuron on a feed-forward neural
network (FNN) processes pixels of the entire image.

124



The way the computer stores and processes images results in numerous parameters of the FNN.



A common FNN cannot resolve image invariance.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Convolutional Neural Networks
⚫

A convolutional neural network (CNN) is a feed-forward neural network. Its artificial neurons can respond to their
surrounding units within a specific coverage. CNNs are great at image processing.

⚫

A CNN consists of a convolution layer, a pooling layer, and a fully connected layer.

⚫

With a CNN, there is no need for complex image pre-processing, as CNN can take the raw images as inputs, which is
one reason they are so popular.

Single Convolution Kernel Calculation
⚫

The values of convolution kernels are the parameter in the convolutional layer. The convolution kernel
scans the entire feature map from left to right and top to bottom, starting in the upper left corner of the
feature map. In each scan, the values at the corresponding positions are multiplied and summed to

obtain a value, which is then placed in the corresponding position of the next feature map.

0

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The green part in the input feature map is filled with 0. This figure shows how to perform
convolution calculation when there are multiple input channels and convolution kernels.
• A convolution kernel slides over the pixels of input images based on predefined rules. The
convolution kernel can extract local features.
• Kernel size: A convolution kernel is a three-dimensional matrix and can be represented by a
cube (w × h × d), where w stands for width, h for height, and d for depth. The depth (d) is
determined by the number of input channels. Generally, only the width (w) and height (h)
are used to describe the kernel size.
• Feature maps are the result of convolution, that is, the process of applying filters to input
images. Each convolution kernel generates a feature map. Multiple convolution kernels
generate a feature map of multiple layers.
• Feature map size: A feature map is also a three-dimensional matrix and can be represented
by a cube (w × h × d), where w stands for width, h for height, and d for depth. The depth
(d) is determined by the number of convolution kernels at the current layer. Generally, only
the width (w) and height (h) are used to describe the feature map size.
• Stride: number of pixels that a convolution kernel moves over an image. If the kernel moves
one pixel at a time, the stride is 1.
• Zero padding: To extract the information on the edges of an image and ensure that the size
of the output feature map meets the requirements, you can pad the edges of the input
image with a border of 0-valued pixels. The width of the border (in pixels) is padding.

⚫

A multi-kernel convolutional layer extracts local image features by using multiple convolution

Pooling Layer
⚫

There are two types of pooling: maximum pooling and average pooling.

⚫

Pooling reduces the number of parameters while keeping the most prominent features,
reduces overfitting, expands receptive fields, and enables invariance.

Core Ideas of CNN – Local Perception (1)
⚫

It is generally believed that the human perception of the outside world starts with specific details and then
extrapolates to the general. Pixels that are in the same area are more closely correlated, whereas pixels far away are
less so.

135

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• It is generally believed that the human perception of the outside world is from partial to
global. Similarly, the spatial relationships in images are such that pixels close to each other
are more tightly connected, whereas pixels that are farther apart have weaker correlations.
Therefore, each neuron does not need to perceive the entire image globally. They only
need to perceive local information. Local information is then integrated at higher layers to
form global information. The idea of local connectivity of the network is also inspired by the
structure of the visual system in biology. Neurons in the visual cortex receive local
information by responding to stimuli within a restricted region.

Core Ideas of CNN – Local Perception (2)
⚫

In a CNN, each neuron only needs to collect information in the local receptive field.

⚫

Advantages:


Less memory is needed.



A CNN simulates how neurons in the visual cortex work. Each neuron collects only local information each time.

Image Invariance
⚫

In the figure on the left, the white blocks indicate pixels whose value is 0, and the orange blocks indicate pixels whose value is 1. No matter where the
highlighted shape is located in the image, it is considered the same one.

⚫

However, when we train a fully connected network with this task, as shown in the figure on the right, the three-dimensional tensor of the image is
flattened into a vector as the input of the network. That is, a 5 × 5 × 1 image (width x height x depth) is displayed as a 25-dimensional vector at the
input layer of the network. When the location of the highlighted shape changes, the vector data varies, causing difficulties to network training and
image recognition.

ILSVRC
⚫

ILSVRC has made significant contribution to the development of deep learning and CNNs.

⚫

ImageNet Large Scale Visual Recognition Challenge, or ILSVRC, is an annual competition held at
Stanford University.

⚫

They use subsets from the ImageNet dataset to run image classification tasks. The dataset used
in the annual ILSVRC challenge includes approximately 1.2 million images and 1,000 categories
of labels. The top-5 and top-1 error rates are used to evaluate the performance of the models.

141

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

ILSVRC Results over the Years
⚫

Since 2010, the annual ILSVRC has included the following three major challenges: image
classification, single object localization, and object detection.

• The annual ILSVRC competition was held for 10 years, and 2012 was a year of
breakthrough. AlexNet won the first place in the 2012 ILSVRC competition, surpassing the
second place by 10.9%. After that, deep learning and convolutional neural networks started
to draw more attention, and researches on deep learning started to gain momentum.
• The debut of AlexNet in ILSVRC 2012 set off a new wave of deep learning around the world.
2012 is also called the first year of deep learning by some in the industry. Since 2012, the
ranking from the ILSVRC competition has become an important standard for measuring the
technical prowess of deep learning research institutes and companies. Even though the
ILSVRC competition has been discontinued, its far-reaching impact and great contribution
to the development of deep learning technology will long be remembered.
• First, it proves the effectiveness of CNNs under complex models. Second, the use of GPUs
allows models to generate results within an acceptable time window, which made both
CNN and GPU hugely popular and also drove the development of supervised DL.

AlexNet Overview
⚫

AlexNet is the network structure that won ILSVRC 2012. AlexNet has only eight layers (not including the input layer),
but it has more than 60 million parameters, more than any of the subsequent networks.

⚫

The earliest AlexNet used a dual-data flow design to address the limitations of early GPUs. Each half of the nodes in

the network are on separate GPUs and multiple GPUs can be used for training.

143

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• CUDA is used to accelerate the training of deep convolutional networks. The powerful
parallel computing capabilities of GPUs are used to process a large number of matrix
operations during neural network training. AlexNet was trained using two GTX 580 GPUs,
each with only 3 GB of GPU memory, which limited the maximum size of the network. The
authors distributed AlexNet across two GPUs and stored half of the neuron parameters in
the memory of each GPU. GPUs can communicate with each other conveniently and access
the memory of each other without using the host memory. Using multiple GPUs
simultaneously is highly effective. Additionally, the design of AlexNet ensures that
communication between GPUs only occurs at certain layers, minimizing performance losses
due to communication overhead.
• ZFNet, the champion of the 2013 ImageNet image classification task, did not introduce
significant structural changes but instead of fine-tuned parameters. Its performance was
greatly improved compared with AlexNet. ZFNet modified the first convolutional layer of
AlexNet, changing the filter size from 11 to 7 and the stride from 4 to 2, and adjusted the
third, fourth, and fifth convolutional layers to 384, 384, and 256 filters, respectively. ZFNet
was not as famous as other classic networks winning ILSVRC competitions held during other
years.

AlexNet Features
⚫

Highlights:


ReLU: Rectified Linear Unit (ReLU) is used instead of the sigmoid activation function for faster
convergence.



Overlapping pooling: The stride is less than the kernel size. This pooling strategy reduces overfitting.



Data augmentation: To prevent overfitting, AlexNet randomly crops the original image (256 × 256)
into a 224 × 224 image, flips it horizontally, and randomly intensifies the illumination.



Dropout: Each neuron in the hidden layers has a probability of 0.5 to output 0. This also prevents
overfitting.

144

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

VGGNet Overview
⚫

VGGNet was proposed by the Visual Geometry Group (VGG) of
Oxford University. VGG16 uses several consecutive 3x3
convolution kernels, instead of the large convolution kernels
(11 × 11 and 5 × 5) used in AlexNet. For a given receptive
field (the size of a local region in the input image, which is

related to the output), using stacked small convolution kernels
is better than using large convolution kernels. This is because
multiple nonlinear layers can increase the network depth to
ensure that more complex patterns can be learned at a
relatively low cost (with fewer parameters).
⚫

Convolutions using simple 3 × 3 convolution kernels and

Decomposition of Convolution Kernels (1)
⚫

One way to decompose convolution kernels is to break down a larger kernel into multiple
smaller kernels.

⚫

In Inception v1, a 5 × 5 convolution consumes a lot of compute, 2.78 times (25/9) that of a 3 ×
3 convolution. Inception V2 borrowed an idea from VGGNet: using two 3 × 3 convolutions
instead of one 5 × 5 convolution.

⚫

Number of two 3 × 3 convolution kernels: 3 × 3 × 2 = 18

⚫

Number of 5 × 5 convolution kernel parameters: 5 × 5= 25

150

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Decomposition of Convolution Kernels (2)
⚫

The second method involves breaking down a symmetric convolutional kernel into multiple asymmetric kernels. For example, a 3 ×
3 convolution kernel can be decomposed into two smaller convolutions, one 1 × 3 and one 3 × 1.

⚫

Decomposing a 3 × 3 convolution into a 1 × 3 and a 3 × 1 convolution results in fewer parameters. A 3 × 3 convolution kernel has
9 parameters, while the combined 1 × 3 and 3 × 1 convolution kernels have only 6 parameters.

⚫

This decomposition method, where an n × n convolution is broken down into 1 × n and n × 1 convolutions, significantly reduces
computational costs as n increases. It has been proven in practice that this decomposition is not very effective in the earlier layers
of a network.

⚫

Both of these decomposition methods reduce compute costs and decrease model overfitting, while also adding a layer of nonlinear expansion to enhance the model's expressive power. The asymmetric convolution structure splitting yields more noticeable
results compared to symmetric splitting into several identical small convolution kernels. This allows for handling more diverse

spatial features, thereby increasing feature diversity.

151

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Residual Structure
⚫

ResNet proposes a structure that can prevent the gradient from vanishing during training. This structure is referred
to as a residual structure.

⚫

The residual module creates a direct connection between the input and output. This way, the newly added network

layers only need to learn new features based on the original input layer, that is, learn the residual, which is relatively
easy.

𝑥
Weight layer
𝐹(𝑥)

153

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In forward propagation, the degradation problem in networks is addressed by using a
residual structure, which makes it easier to learn redundant layers.
• During backward propagation, the error signal can be directly transmitted to lower layers
without passing through any intermediate weight matrix transformations, alleviating the
gradient vanishing problem to some extent.
• In ResNet v2, the positions of Batch Normalization (BN) and ReLU activation are different.

Two Forms of Residual Blocks
⚫

Identity blocks: The input and output dimensions in an identity block are the same. This allows for easy stacking of multiple identity blocks.

⚫

Convolutional blocks: The input and output dimensions in a convolutional block are different. This difference is intentionally designed to change the
dimensionality of the feature vector.

• In both block functions, input_tensor undergoes several Conv2D, Batch Normalization, and
ReLU operations to produce x, and then the Addition operation is performed with the
shortcut. The difference lies in the nature of the shortcut: in the identity block, the shortcut
is input_tensor, while in the conv block, the shortcut is obtained after input_tensor passes
through Conv2d and Batch Normalization layers. These two types of blocks thus implement
two different forms of shortcut connections.

• The previous best result was 2.991%. SENet was the champion model of ILSVRC 2017. It
reduced the top-5 error on the ImageNet dataset to 2.251%, surpassing the previous best
result of 2.991%.
• SENet consists of two parts: Squeeze and Excitation.
• The innovation of the SENet network lies in its focus on the relationships between channels,
allowing the model to automatically learn the importance of different channel features.
• Essentially, the SE module performs attention operations on the channel dimension. This
attention mechanism enables the model to focus more on the most informative channel
features while suppressing less important ones.
• The SE module is versatile, meaning it can be embedded into existing network
architectures.

Main Algorithms for Object Detection
⚫

Object detection identifies, locates, and categorizes objects of interest in images. Object detection
algorithms are classified into the following types:


Traditional object detection algorithms: Cascade, HOG/DPM, Haar/SVM and many improvements and

optimizations of the foregoing methods


Deep learning algorithms:
◼

Two-stage algorithms: Region proposals (RP) are first identified, and then CNN-based classification (RCNN series) is
performed. Common two-stage object detection algorithms include R-CNN, SPP-Net, Fast R-CNN, Faster R-CNN, and RFCN.

◼

One-stage algorithms: Features are extracted from images using a network, and then the extracted features are used to
predict object classification and location. Common one-stage object detection algorithms include OverFeat, YOLO series,
SSD, and RetinaNet.

157

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Two-Stage Object Detection Methods
⚫

Traditional object detection methods require you to manually design feature extraction factors and then feed the extracted features into an SVM for
classification and regression. The effectiveness of detection mainly depends on the quality of the feature factors.

⚫

With the emergence of deep learning, convolutional neural networks (CNNs) have enabled automatic feature extraction, greatly improving detection
performance. This advancement has resulted in the development of two-stage object detection algorithms. These algorithms initially generate
candidate bounding boxes and then refine their positions and predict their classes. Examples include the RCNN series and Pyramid Networks.

Extract candidate
bounding boxes.

Images

CNNs replace traditional machine learning models.

158

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Extract
features.

Classify and regress
candidate bounding
boxes.

Single-Stage Object Detection Methods
⚫

To adapt to real-time inference scenarios and further improve detection speed, candidate bounding box extraction is
eliminated. Entire images are directly detected and classified. This approach is known as one-stage object detection.
Common one-stage algorithms include the YOLO series and RetinaNet, which are known for their strong real-time
performance and high accuracy.

GAN Overview
⚫

First proposed by Goodfellow et al., in 2014, Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs) are one of the most popular
generative models in recent years. GANs consist of two competing networks: a generator and a discriminator.
Originally, GANs aimed to learn the actual data distribution and generate images that were similar but not identical
to those in datasets.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• GANs can be trained using optimizers based on well-established gradient descent
algorithms, such as the Adam optimizer. During training, the backpropagation algorithm can
be used to update parameters. It is important to note that, unlike other deep learning
models, the generator and discriminator have different objectives, so they need to be
trained separately. Additionally, since the generator initially produces low-quality images,
such as noise, and the discriminator can only distinguish between noise and real images,
the generator and discriminator need to be trained alternately. They essentially chase and
catch up to each other, evolving together.

Training the Discriminator
The goal of training the discriminator is to distinguish between real images and generated images. Specifically, when the input
image is a real image, we want the output to be as close to "1" as possible. Conversely, when the input image is a generated image,
we want the output to be as close to "0" as possible. When training the discriminator, we need to fix the parameters of the
generator. If the generator's parameters are not fixed, it could reduce the quality of the generated images to "assist" the
discriminator in making distinctions.

163

Sample
Real

Loss

images

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

update discriminator
weights

Training the Generator
The goal of training the generator is to "fool" the discriminator, so that the discriminator cannot distinguish between
real and generated images. Specifically, when a generated image is input into the discriminator, we want the output
to be as close to "1" as possible. When training the generator, we need to fix the parameters of the discriminator. If
the discriminator's parameters are not fixed, its discrimination performance can deteriorate. It can start treating all
images as real.

Problems in GAN Training – Underfitting and Overfitting
⚫

Underfitting and overfitting in GANs


GAN underfitting: The network is unable to generate high-quality images. This has been a longstanding challenge in GAN research, where improving the quality of generated images is a key focus.

One significant reason for underfitting is the insufficient generative capacity of the model. To address
underfitting, we can try increasing the number of hidden layers and neurons in the original network.
Additionally, changing the network structure can help, such as using Deep Convolutional Generative
Adversarial Networks (DCGANs).


GAN overfitting: The generated images are identical to, or are just translations of, the images in the

dataset. We can mitigate overfitting by increasing the size of the training dataset and using
techniques like Dropout.

165

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Problems During GAN Training – Mode Collapse
⚫

Mode collapse


Mode collapse is a problem unique to GANs, where the model fails to generate diverse images. For
example, if we use the MNIST dataset and aim to generate images of digits from "0" to "9", the

generator might "lazily" produce only easy-to-generate digits, such as "1", while avoiding more
complex digits like "8". Intuitively, we can understand that as long as the generator produces highquality images of "1", it can still "fool" the discriminator.


Mode collapse remains an unsolved issue. Fortunately, many research papers have proposed various
methods to mitigate it, such as VEEGAN, AdaGAN, and MAD-GAN.

166

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Problems During GAN Training – Instability
⚫

Instability


Vanishing Gradients: When GAN training is just starting, vanishing gradients can be a common issue.
This occurs when the discriminator is either too good or too poor at its task, making it difficult for the

generator to continue training effectively.


Poor convergence: In the later stages of GAN training, the generator may find it hard to converge on a
solution.

⚫

Many research papers have proposed modifying the objective functions of GANs to address
these issues. Examples include LSGAN, WGAN, and WGAN-GP.

167

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Mitigating Training Instability
⚫

Two techniques to mitigate GAN training instability:


Single-sided label smoothing: When training the discriminator, set the labels for real images to 0.9
instead of 1. This can prevent the discriminator from having excessively large gradients, ensuring that

it does not become "too good" at the beginning of the training process.


Separating batches for real and generated images: When training the discriminator, add either real
images or generated images to each batch, rather than shuffling and mixing them. This approach can
also help alleviate training instability.

168

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The techniques prevent the discriminator from becoming too good at its task, which could
lead to vanishing gradients and make it impossible to train the generator effectively.

DCGAN Overview
⚫

The Deep Convolutional Generative Adversarial Network (DCGAN) is a generative model
proposed by Alec Radford et al., in 2016. This model improves upon the original GAN structure
by replacing multi-layer perceptron with a convolutional neural network structure, enabling the

model to generate higher-quality images.

169

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

DCGAN Structure
⚫

We already know that the discriminator model essentially performs a classification task. We can construct the discriminator in a DCGAN similar to the
LeNet-5 convolutional neural network. It performs binary classification on generated and real images using convolution, pooling (down-sampling), and
fully connected layers.

⚫

The input to the discriminator model is an image, and the output is a scalar. It uses convolution and down-sampling in the convolutional neural
network for classification. The generator, on the other hand, uses low-dimensional noise as input, and then produces high-dimensional images,
requiring transposed convolution or upsampling to "enlarge" the images.

The shadow part represents the transposed convolution kernel

Original feature map
170

Feature map after
transposed
convolution

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Transposed convolution is the inverse operation of convolution, but essentially, it is still
performing convolution operations. Specifically, the previous layer's feature map
undergoes a specific padding, and then the convolution kernel values are mirrored
symmetrically before performing convolution calculations.
• In the generator model, upsampling followed by regular convolution layers can also be
used. Upsampling essentially involves replicating the values of the original feature map
along rows and columns multiple times.

CGAN Overview
⚫

Conditional Generative Adversarial Network (CGAN) was first proposed by Mehdi Mirza et al., in
2014. The main difference from the original GAN is its ability to control the generated images
by adding text or images. However, achieving this requires supervised learning, meaning

labeled datasets are needed for training. For example, the earliest CGAN was able to generate
corresponding handwritten digit images with the digits 0 to 9 provided as conditions.

171

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

GAN Review
⚫

First, let's review the structure of the original GAN. The input to the generator is noise, while
the input to the discriminator consists of both generated images and real images from the
dataset. It can be observed that during the entire training process, only the images from the

dataset are used, and these images do not need labels.

CGAN Structure
⚫

In a CGAN, the input to the discriminator not only includes images from the dataset but also the corresponding
labels. For the generator, the input includes not only noise but also the labels of the images to be generated. The
generated images, along with the specified labels, are then fed into the discriminator, which outputs the evaluation
results.

• The discriminator in a CGAN not only needs to consider whether the generated image is
close to a real image, but also whether the generated image matches the label.
• The label does not necessarily have to be a noun; it can also be a descriptive sentence.
However, the sentence needs to be processed appropriately for input into the network,
such as converting it into word vectors.

Combining Labels and Images
⚫

In a CGAN, the discriminator's input requires not only images but also labels. How are the images and labels
combined to form the input? In the earliest CGAN, the authors converted both the labels and images into vectors
and concatenated these vectors to form a longer vector. This longer vector was then used as the input.

• If you want to build a CGAN using convolutional layers, besides multiplying the vectors, you
can also try converting the label vectors into matrices (of the same size as the noise or
image) and concatenating them with the noise or image along the channel dimension.
Multiplying or adding the label vectors and image vectors is not without basis; in the selfattention layer, position matrices and word vector matrices are fused by adding them
together.

Pix2Pix Overview
⚫

Like CGAN, Pix2Pix also performs supervised learning. However, in Pix2Pix, both labels and data
are images, enabling image-to-image translation. Pix2Pix can accomplish various tasks such as
transforming day to night, converting outlines to images, and coloring images.

• In the original paper, the authors only used dropout as a source of uncertainty and did not
add noise to the labels.
• It can be observed that when training the generator, the objective function needs to
consider not only "fooling" the discriminator but also the L1 loss between the generated
image and the original image. This is because considering only the CGAN loss may not
produce high-quality images, potentially generating objects that do not exist in the original
labels or real images. Therefore, the authors proposed combining the CGAN loss with the L1
loss to achieve better results.
• Additionally, in tasks such as street scene translation, considering only the CGAN loss may
fail to generate details like parking lines. By combining CGAN loss with L1 loss, more details
can be generated.

WGAN Overview
⚫

A Wasserstein GAN (WGAN) introduces a "Wasserstein distance" to redefine the similarity
measure in the GAN models. The Wasserstein distance, also known as the Earth-Mover (EM)
distance, is used to measure the distance between two distributions.

EM:
⚫
One distribution P is considered as a pile of earth and
⚫

179

another distribution Q as the target.
The distance d is the average distance a bulldozer
needs to move the earth pile.

P

Q

d

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The original GAN function is actually based on two important similarity measures: KullbackLeibler divergence (KL divergence) and Jensen-Shannon divergence (JS divergence).
However, there is a problem when KL divergence and JS divergence are measured. If two
distributions P and Q are far apart and have no overlap, the KL divergence is meaningless.
During learning, this means that the gradient at this point is 0, that is, the gradient vanishes.
Therefore, the authors of WGAN introduced the Wasserstein distance to redefine the
similarity measure in GAN models. The Wasserstein distance, also known as Earth-Mover
(EM) distance, is used to measure the distance between two distributions.

technology.

Introduction to Speech Processing
Speech signal processing, also known as speech processing, is a term used to study various processing techniques in

⚫

the speech production process, the statistical characteristics of speech signals, automatic speech recognition,
machine synthesis, and speech perception.
Modern speech processing technology is based on digital computation and is implemented using microprocessors,

⚫

signal processors, or general-purpose computers, hence it is also called digital speech signal processing.

Language information is mainly contained in the parameters of the speech signal, so accurately and quickly

⚫

extracting the parameters of the speech signal is the key to speech signal processing.

Phonetics (1)
Phonetics is a branch of linguistics that studies the sounds of human language. It mainly investigates the

⚫

mechanisms of speech production, phonetic characteristics, and the patterns of change in speech.
Narrowly defined, phonetics corresponds to the English term "phonetics", which focuses on the essence of specific

⚫

sounds and the methods of sound production. In contrast, phonology (or phonemics) studies the abstract rules of
phoneme or phonetic feature operations within a language and the phonetic system.

Broadly defined, phonetics encompasses both phonetics and phonology.

⚫

Essence of specific sounds and the
methods of sound production

Phonetics

Linguistics
Phonetic characteristics and the
patterns of change in speech

7

Phonology

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Since the study of phonetics involves the actions of pronunciation, the characteristics of
vocal sounds, and auditory perception, and different language communities have their
own phonetic characteristics, modern phonetic research needs to be based on both
natural science and social science knowledge.

Phonetics (2)
Phonetics can be roughly divided into four major types, covering the entire process of sound production to

⚫

reception:


Articulatory phonetics: Studies how speech sounds are produced by the speech organs in the oral cavity (e.g., lips, teeth,
tongue, vocal cords).



Acoustic phonetics: Studies the acoustic analysis of speech sounds, such as the frequency, duration, and amplitude of sound

waves.

8



Auditory phonetics: Studies how the human ear receives sounds, i.e., the auditory perception of speech by the ear.



Linguistic phonetics: Combines sound, social environment, personal habits, and language rules to study speech sounds.
◼

Different people in the same region may pronounce the same word or phrase differently.

◼

People from different regions in the same country may pronounce the same word or phrase very differently.

◼

The same person may pronounce the same word or phrase differently in different contexts or emotional states.

◼

The same word or phrase may have different pronunciations in different contexts.

Speech Data
⚫

Speech refers to sound that carries linguistic information, comprising both acoustic and linguistic
elements.

⚫

Characteristics of speech signals:


Speech signals change over time, making them non-stationary, time-varying signals. However, due to the
influence of the oral muscles during speech production, speech signals are relatively stable over short periods,
appearing as quasi-stationary processes. Therefore, speech signals exhibit short-term stationarity.



Short-term analysis techniques are essential throughout the entire process of speech signal analysis.



Speech is produced by the movement of oral muscles, whose motion is much slower compared to speech
frequency.



10

The short-term range is generally considered to be 10-30 milliseconds.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Signal Preprocessing
⚫

Speech files are typically in WAV format. The following figure visualizes an audio file, with the horizontal axis
representing the number of sample points and the vertical axis representing the amplitude.

⚫

First, the audio signal needs to be preprocessed. The main issues with the illustrated audio signal are:

11



Uneven distribution of waveform data.



Silent portions at the beginning and end.



Noise presents in the waveform.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The horizontal axis represents the number of sample points, and the vertical axis
represents amplitude.
• The distribution of waveform data is very uneven, with some waveforms appearing near
the end of the audio, some in the middle, and some at the beginning.
• There is a long period of silence at the beginning and end.
• Some WAV files have small waves in areas other than the main waveform, which are
likely to be external noise.

Speech Signal Preprocessing Steps
⚫

Speech signal preprocessing generally includes:


Digitization: Discretizing the analog speech signals collected from sensors into digital signals.



Pre-emphasis: The purpose of pre-emphasis is to boost the high-frequency components of the speech signal,
eliminating the effects of lip radiation and increasing the high-frequency resolution of the speech signal.



Endpoint detection: Identifying and eliminating long silent segments from the speech signal, reducing
environmental interference with the signal.



Framing: Due to the short-term stationarity of speech, "short-term analysis" is required, i.e., dividing the signal
into segments, each segment is called a frame (usually 10-30 ms).



Windowing: Framing of the speech signal is achieved by applying a weighted method using a movable finitelength window. The purpose of windowing is to reduce the truncation effect of the speech frame. Common
windows include rectangular window, Hanning window, and Hamming window.

12

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Signal Preprocessing - Pre-Emphasis
Lip radiation: Lip radiation can cause energy loss, which is more pronounced in the high-frequency range and less in
the low-frequency range. Therefore, to eliminate the influence, a high-pass filter can be used for pre-emphasis to
enhance the high-frequency resolution.
Original speech signal spectrum

Speech Signal Preprocessing - Framing
⚫

Framing: Dividing variable-length audio into fixed-length segments.


Although framing can be done using continuous segmentation, overlapping segmentation is generally used to ensure smooth
transitions between frames and maintain continuity. The overlapping portion between the previous frame and the subsequent
frame is called frame shift.

Window size

Frame shift
Overlapping portion
14

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Typically, the frame length is 20 to 50 ms, and the frame shift is 10 ms.

Speech Signal Preprocessing - Windowing
Windowing: After framing, breaks occur at the beginning and end of each frame. Therefore, the more segmented the frames, the
greater the error from the original signal. Windowing solves this problem by making the framed signal continuous, and each frame
exhibits the characteristics of a periodic function.


Different window functions affect the results of speech signal analysis. The rectangular window provides better smoothness but loses waveform
details and creates leakage, while the Hamming window can effectively alleviate leakage and is the most widely used.
Rectangular window timedomain waveform

Hamming window timedomain waveform

amplitude characteristics

Hamming window amplitude
characteristics

Amplitude (dB)

⚫

Number of samples

Normalized frequency (f/fs)

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The main lobe width of the rectangular window is smaller than that of the Hamming
window, providing higher spectral resolution. However, the peak value of the side lobes
in the rectangular window is higher, which causes more severe spectral leakage. In
comparison, although the main lobe width of the Hamming window is wider,
approximately twice that of the rectangular window, its side lobes attenuate more
significantly. This results in a smoother low-pass characteristic, which can more
accurately reflect the frequency characteristics of short-term signals.

Speech Features (1)
⚫

When analyzing a speech file, certain measures are needed to effectively reflect the essence of the
speech, much like the importance of features in machine learning. Therefore, the design of speech
features is critical for speech processing.

⚫

Speech features describe core information about the speech and play an important role in constructing
speech models.

⚫

Key speech features:

17



Contain effective information to distinguish phonemes: Good time-domain and frequency-domain resolution.



Separate fundamental frequency (F0) and its harmonic components.



Robust to different speakers.



Robust to noise or channel distortion.



Good pattern recognition characteristics: Low-dimensional features, feature independence.

Speech Signal Analysis (1)
⚫

In a narrow sense, speech signal analysis does not include the process of pre-processing, such as denoising and smoothing the
speech signal. However, these two processes are usually collectively referred to as speech signal analysis.

⚫

Importance of speech signal analysis:


The quality of synthesized speech and the accuracy of speech recognition largely depend on the accuracy and precision of speech signal analysis.



Speech signal analysis is the foundation and prerequisite for technologies like speech synthesis, speech recognition, speech enhancement, and

target speech extraction. Only with accurate and targeted analysis of speech features can these technologies be better supported, allowing them
to perform effectively in different use cases.

Time-Domain Analysis of Speech Signals
⚫

Time-domain analysis of speech signals involves analyzing and extracting time-domain parameters of speech signals.
This is one of the earliest and most widely used methods (as speech signals themselves are time-domain signals). It
is commonly used for basic parameter analysis and applications such as speech segmentation, preprocessing, and
broad classification. Its characteristics include:

⚫



Clear physical significance and intuitiveness, allowing the extraction of some important parameters in speech.



Simple to implement.

Time-domain parameters of speech signals:

21



Short-term energy.



Short-term zero-crossing rate.



Short-term autocorrelation function.



Short-term average magnitude difference function.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Frequency-Domain Analysis of Speech Signals
⚫

Frequency-domain analysis of speech signals involves analyzing and extracting frequencydomain parameters of speech signals.

⚫

The most commonly used method for frequency-domain analysis is the Fourier analysis
method. Since speech signals are non-stationary processes, short-time Fourier transform is

required for spectral analysis of speech signals. By observing the spectrum of speech signals,
one can identify their formant characteristics, fundamental frequency, and harmonic
frequencies.

22

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Features
⚫

recognition are the MFCC.

⚫









DFT

Waveform

MFCC

log

triangular band-pass filters


23

Cepstral analysis (taking logarithm and performing inverse transform)

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Why log transformation? It is because human ears' sensitivity to sound loudness is not
linear. The cochlea acts as a set of filters, exhibiting a linear response below 1,000 Hz
and a logarithmic response above 1,000 Hz. Human ears are more sensitive to lowfrequency signals. Taking the logarithm reduces the disparity between small and large
signals. Initially, a disparity of 10^5 times can be reduced to 100 dB after logarithmic
transformation. Comparing 100 and 10^5, the gap is significantly minimized, making
analysis and processing easier. Without taking the logarithm, small signals might be
overwhelmed by large signals. This process is similar to normalization.

Speech Recognition
⚫

Speech recognition technology enables machines to convert speech signals into corresponding
text or commands by recognizing and understanding them.

⚫

Fields involved in speech recognition technology: signal processing, pattern recognition,
probability theory and information theory, voice mechanism and auditory mechanism, AI, and

more.
Input

Output

"I love you."

25

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Status Quo of Speech Recognition
⚫

Speech recognition is a type of perceptual intelligence within AI. Its applications have already
penetrated various fields, such as home appliances, communications, automobiles, healthcare,
and household services, for example, voice assistants, robots, and smart speakers.

⚫

At present, the accuracy of AI speech recognition has surpassed that of humans. Thanks to the

development of foundation models, speech models can achieve multi-lingual and multi-domain
language recognition, as well as speech synthesis, among other functions.
⚫

However, limited by current speech sampling devices and datasets, speech recognition still
faces some issues and cannot completely reach human levels (such as recognizing dialects or in
noisy environments).

26

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Challenges in Speech Recognition
⚫

⚫

Challenges of speech recognition tasks:


Regionality



Contextuality



Physiological factors

Cocktail party problem: When multiple speakers' speech signals overlap, it becomes difficult for
machines to separate them into individual signals, leading to a significant decline in recognition
performance.

⚫

To sum up, the challenges of speech recognition in one sentence: it is highly uncertain. The
same word or sentence might sound completely different due to various factors.

27

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Regionality: A person from Sichuan saying "I love you", a person from Hunan saying "I
love you", and a person from Jiangxi saying "I love you" might pronounce the same
sentence differently, sometimes even very differently. This regional variation presents
significant challenges for speech recognition.
• Contextuality: Consider how we might say the same sentence in different settings. Our
tone and intonation might change depending on the situation and the person we're
speaking to. Additionally, our mood can affect how we say something - saying a sentence
when happy versus when sad can sound different too. These variations introduce
challenges stemming from context and emotion.
• Physiological factors: Another major factor is individual differences in timbre and
pronunciation habits. Even if the same consonants and vowels are used, the sound
waves produced by different people can vary, making speech recognition more complex.

Classification of Speech Recognition Tasks - Isolated Word
Recognition
⚫

Isolated word recognition: In the early stages of speech processing development, the focus was
on recognizing a small number of isolated words:


The input speech file contains only one word (after segmenting a full sentence input), and then the
model identifies which word the file belongs to. Commonly used models for this task include GMMHMM, where each word is modeled individually.
Input

Output
"0"
"2"

...
"9"
28

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Classification of Speech Recognition Tasks - Continuous Word
Recognition
⚫

Continuous word recognition: In practice, recognizing a small number of isolated words is not sufficient to meet
actual needs. Most requirements involve recognizing continuous sentences. Using isolated word recognition
algorithms for this purpose presents several issues:


Entire files must be segmented into isolated words, which requires significant manual effort and cannot ensure accuracy, as the
pronunciation of many words is connected.



Even if perfect segmentation is achieved, the number of words required in actual usage is very large. The
matching strategy used in isolated word recognition offers no advantages here and might even become a
disadvantage due to the vast vocabulary.
"I love you."
"The weather is so nice today."
...

Speech Synthesis
⚫

Speech synthesis, also known as TTS technology, converts any text information into
corresponding speech output.

⚫

Speech synthesis involves multiple disciplines, including acoustics, linguistics, digital signal
processing, and computer science.

⚫

To synthesize high-quality speech, it relies not only on various rules, including semantic, lexical,
and phonological rules, but also requires a good understanding of the text content, which
involves natural language understanding.

34

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Synthesis System
⚫

A complete speech synthesis system first converts a text sequence into a phonemic sequence,
and then generates a speech waveform based on the phonemic sequence.


The first step involves linguistic processing, such as word segmentation, character-to-sound
conversion, and a set of effective prosody control rules.



The second step requires advanced speech synthesis technology to synthesize high-quality speech
streams in real-time as required.

⚫

Speech synthesis technology research has a history of over 200 years. However, the truly
practical modern speech synthesis technology has developed with the advancements in
computer technology and digital signal processing technology, primarily aiming to enable
computers to produce high-definition, highly natural continuous speech.
35

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Text Analysis
⚫

In speech synthesis, the main task of text analysis is converting text data into a phonemic
internal representation. Specific tasks include:


Text normalization: Preprocessing or normalizing various natural text data, including lemmatization,
disambiguation of non-standard words, homographs, etc.



Speech analysis: Following text normalization, speech analysis involves methods such as using largescale pronunciation lexicons and grapheme-to-phoneme conversion rules.



37

Prosody analysis: Analyzing the prosodic structure, prominence, and intonation in the text.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Synthesis Methods
⚫

Throughout the development of speech synthesis technology, early research primarily used parametric synthesis methods, later
followed by waveform concatenative synthesis with the advancement of computer technology.

⚫

Parametric synthesis


Early research on speech synthesis primarily used parametric synthesis methods. Notably, Holmes' parallel formant synthesizer (1973) and Klatt's
serial/parallel formant synthesizer (1980) could produce very natural speech when parameters were carefully adjusted. However, accurately
extracting formant parameters was challenging, making the synthesized speech quality difficult to meet practical demands.

⚫

Waveform concatenative synthesis


Since the late 1980s, language synthesis technology has made new progress, especially with the introduction of the pitch-synchronous overlapadd (PSOLA) method (1990). This significantly improved the timbre and naturalness of speech synthesized using the time-domain waveform
concatenative method. The naturalness exceeded that of previous LPC or formant synthesizer-based methods. PSOLA-based synthesizers have a
simpler structure, are easier to implement in real-time, and hold substantial commercial potential.

38

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Synthesis Algorithms

⚫

⚫

Definition of GMM
⚫

A GMM uses Gaussian probability density functions (normal distribution curves) to quantize
things accurately. It decomposes things into several models based on Gaussian probability
density functions.

43

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Gaussian Distribution
⚫

The Gaussian distribution, also known as the normal distribution, was first derived by de Moivre while working on
the asymptotic formula for binomial distribution. It was later obtained from another perspective by Gauss while
studying measurement errors. It is a significant probability distribution in fields like mathematics, physics, and
engineering, greatly influencing many aspects of statistics.

⚫

If a random variable X follows a normal distribution with a mean 𝜇 and variance 𝜎 2 , it is denoted as 𝑁(𝜇, 𝜎 2 ). Its

probability density function is determined by the normal distribution's mean 𝜇, defining its position, and standard
deviation 𝜎, defining the amplitude. When 𝜇 = 0 and 𝜎 = 1, it is a standard normal distribution with the following
formula:
(𝑥−𝜇)2

Introduction of Maximum Likelihood Method
⚫

The maximum likelihood method (ML) or maximum likelihood estimation (MLE) is a theoretically-based
point estimation method. It is a statistical method used to find the parameters of a probability density
function associated with a sample set.

⚫

The basic idea is that after randomly drawing 𝑛 sample observations from the model population, the
most reasonable parameter estimation should maximize the probability of obtaining these 𝑛 sample
observations from the model, unlike the least squares estimation method, which aims to obtain
parameter estimates that best fit the sample data to the model.
Known
1. The distribution model
of the sample
2. Randomly drawn
samples

47

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Unknown
MLE

Model parameters

Maximum Likelihood Estimation
⚫

Assume there are 𝑁 independent data points, each following a certain distribution 𝑃𝑟(𝑥; 𝜃). We aim to find a set of parameters 𝜃
that maximizes the probability of generating these data points. This probability is expressed as:
𝑁

ෑ 𝑃𝑟(𝑥𝑖 ; 𝜃)
𝑖=1
⚫

This is known as the likelihood function. Usually, the probability for a single point is very small, resulting in even smaller values

when multiplied together, which can cause floating-point underflow. Hence, we generally take the logarithm, transforming it into:
𝑁

෍ 𝑙𝑜𝑔𝑃𝑟(𝑥𝑖 ; 𝜃)
𝑖=1
⚫

This is called the log-likelihood function. Then, we can take the derivative and solve for the parameters 𝜃 that maximize the value of
this expression. While it is unlikely that these observations occurred with high probability, the parameters 𝜃 make it most likely that
they did.

48

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Single Gaussian Model Parameter Learning
⚫

For a single Gaussian model, we can estimate the parameter 𝜃 using the MLE method. The parameter 𝜃 is found by maximizing the
likelihood function 𝜃 = 𝑎𝑟𝑔𝑚𝑎𝑥𝜃 𝐿(𝜃). Here, we assume that each data point is independent, and the likelihood function is given
by the probability density function:
𝑁

𝐿 𝜃 = ෑ 𝑃(𝑥𝑗 |𝜃)
𝑗=1
⚫

Since the probability of each point is very small, the product can become extremely small, making computation and observation
difficult. Therefore, we usually use the maximum log-likelihood instead. The log function's monotonicity ensures that it does not
change the position of the extrema, and small changes in input values between 0 and 1 can cause relatively large changes in output
values:
𝑁

𝑙𝑜𝑔𝐿 𝜃 = ෍ 𝑙𝑜𝑔𝑃(𝑥𝑗 |𝜃)
𝑗=1

49

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Gaussian Distribution Model Parameter Estimation
⚫

For a sample dataset, we use the Gaussian probability distribution to fit this dataset, and the
steps to solve Gaussian distribution model parameters follow these steps:


Use the Gaussian probability density function.



Write the likelihood function based on sample data and the form of the Gaussian probability

distribution.

50



Transform the likelihood function into a log-likelihood function.



Derive the log-likelihood function concerning the parameters and set the equation to zero.



Solve for the optimal parameter values.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The above content describes how to use MLE to solve for the probability distribution
function of a sample dataset.
• For a sample dataset, if we use Gaussian probability distribution to fit this dataset, the
steps to solve for the Gaussian distribution model parameters are the same.
• The detailed steps are:
▫ Use the Gaussian probability density function.
▫ Write the likelihood function based on sample data and the form of the Gaussian
probability distribution.
▫ Transform the likelihood function into a log-likelihood function.
▫ Derive the log-likelihood function concerning the parameters and set the equation
to zero.

▫ Solve for the optimal parameter values.
• Thus, the entire parameter estimation process is completed.

GMM
⚫

A GMM is an extension of a single Gaussian probability density function. It can smoothly
approximate the density distribution of any shape. There are two types of Gaussian mixture
models: single Gaussian model (SGM) and Gaussian mixture model (GMM).

⚫

Similar to clustering, each Gaussian model can be seen as a category based on different

parameters of the probability density function (PDF). Given an input sample 𝑥, its value can be
computed using the PDF, then judged whether it belongs to the Gaussian model based on a
threshold. SGM is suitable for binary classification, while GMM, with multiple models, provides
finer segmentation and can be used for multi-category classification and complex object
modeling.

51

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• In general, a mixture model can use any probability distribution. The Gaussian mixture
model is used here because the Gaussian distribution has excellent mathematical
properties and good computational performance.

Mathematical Definition of GMM
⚫

The probability distribution of a Gaussian mixture model:
𝐾

𝑃 𝑥 𝜃 = ෍ 𝛼𝑘 𝜙(𝑥|𝜃𝑘 )
𝑘=1
⚫

How do we estimate the parameters for a GMM? Unlike a single Gaussian model, we cannot directly use
MLE and take the derivative to find parameters that maximize the likelihood because we do not know in
advance which sub-distribution each observation belongs to (hidden variable). The log term includes a
summation, and the sum of the 𝐾 Gaussian models is not a single Gaussian model, making it impossible
to compute directly through derivatives for each sub-model's unknown parameters (𝛼𝑘 , 𝜇𝑘 , 𝜎𝑘 ). This
requires an iterative method to solve it.

53

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

EM Algorithm
⚫

The expectation maximization (EM) algorithm is an iterative algorithm used for maximum likelihood
estimation or maximum a posteriori estimation in probabilistic models with hidden variables.

⚫

The EM algorithm was proposed by Dempster, Laird, and Rubin in 1977 as a method for finding
maximum likelihood estimation parameters. It can perform MLE estimation on parameters from
incomplete data sets and is a very simple and practical learning algorithm. This method can be widely
applied to handle missing data, censored data, and so-called incomplete data with noise.
Known

samples

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Steps of the EM Algorithm (3)
⚫

57

1.

Initialize parameters.

2.

Expectation: Calculate the probability of each data point belonging to each single Gaussian model.

3.

Maximization: Update parameters based on the expectation results.

4.

Iterate the above process until convergence.

Markov Chain Case Solution
⚫

⚫

Markov Chain
⚫

A Markov chain is a discrete-event stochastic process with the Markov property in mathematics. In this
process, given the current knowledge or information, the past is irrelevant for predicting the future, only
the current state matters.

⚫

In each step of a Markov chain, the system can transition from one state to another, or remain in the
current state, based on a probability distribution. This state change is called a transition, and the
probability associated with different state changes is called the transition probability.

Markov Chain Principle
⚫

Principle:


A Markov chain describes a sequence of states where each state value depends on a finite number of prior
states. A Markov chain is a sequence of random variables with the Markov property. The range of these
variables, known as the set of all possible values, is called the "state space".

⚫

Properties:


Positivity: Each element in the state transition matrix is referred to as a state transition probability. According to
probability theory, each state transition probability is a positive number, and the formula can be expressed as:
𝑝𝑖𝑗 (𝑘) ≥ 0.



Finiteness: According to probability theory, the sum of each row in the state transition matrix equals 1, which
can be expressed with the formula:
෍ 𝑝𝑖𝑗 = 1

63

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Observable Markov Model
⚫

For a problem, we have the initial distribution 𝜋 and the transition probability matrix 𝐴. At any
given time 𝑡, we have a state 𝑂𝑡 . The state transitions over time to another state, generating an
observable sequence, which is the state sequence 𝑂 = [𝑜1 , 𝑜2 , 𝑜3 , 𝑜4 , … , 𝑜𝑛 ]. There are a
total of 𝑛 observed states in the entire problem.

⚫

The probability of such a sequence occurring is:
𝑚

𝑃 𝑂 𝐴, 𝜋 = 𝑃(𝑜1 ) ෑ 𝑃(𝑜𝑡 |𝑜𝑡−1 )
𝑡=2
⚫

Thus, an observable Markov model is represented by a triplet (𝐴, 𝜋, 𝑛) and can often be
simplified as 𝐴, 𝜋 .
64

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Markov Chain Learning Problem
⚫

Markov model learning


In the case of a phenomenon, nobody will tell us the parameters of the Markov model in advance. Therefore, if
we want to study this random process, we must learn the parameters from the available data.



The Markov model learning problem involves learning the parameters of the Markov model given a series of
observed data.



The learning content includes the initial probability 𝜋 and the transition probability matrix A. The state set is
predetermined during the problem study and does not require additional learning.

Markov Chain Learning Algorithm - Exhaustive Method
⚫

Exhaustive method: In learning the Markov model, we use the exhaustive method, also known as the probability
approximation method. The more sample sequence data we obtain, the higher the accuracy of the parameters.

state set 𝑆.

⚫

Application: Using Markov model prediction, we can anticipate the likelihood of a sequence occurring
and identify which Markov model generated an observed sequence.



J's recreational activities are influenced by his mood on the day, and the probability of choosing these activities varies with his
mood. For example, when he is "happy", the probability of watching TV is high, and when he is "unhappy", the probability of
playing football is higher.

J's daily mood state is hidden (the quality of his mood cannot be directly observed), but his recreational activities

can be directly observed. Hence, we usually define:


The state that cannot be directly observed as the hidden state (J's mood).



The state that can be directly observed as the observable state (J's recreational activities).

HMM Case Introduction (3)
⚫

⚫

Suppose we want to delve into the following problem:



There are two states: hidden and observable states.



The current hidden state determines the probability distribution of the current observable state.



The distribution of the next time step's hidden state is influenced only by the current hidden state.

We model this dual stochastic process mathematically as the HMM.
71

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

HMM (1)
⚫

An HMM is essentially an extension of the standard Markov model, incorporating a set of observable
states and the probabilistic relationship between these states and hidden states.

⚫

Similar to the three elements of the Markov model, the HMM is uniquely determined by five key
elements.

Hidden state set S

Hidden state transition
probability set A

72

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Observable state set R

Initial probability π

Emission probability B

HMM (2)
⚫

An HMM can be described using five elements:


Hidden state set : 𝑅 = 𝑅1 , 𝑅2 , 𝑅3,…, 𝑅𝑚 ; for example, J's mood states such as happy, unhappy, neutral.



Observable state set : S= 𝑆1 , 𝑆2 , 𝑆3,…, 𝑆𝑛 ; for example, J's recreational activities such as playing football, listening to music,
watching TV.



Initial probability: 𝜋 = 𝑃𝑖𝑛𝑖 𝑆𝑖 ∀ i ∈ 1, 𝑛 }; for example, J's initial mood, generally considered as a hypothesized value at
the beginning of a random sequence, like assuming J's mood starts from scratch at the beginning of each month, unaffected by
the previous month.



Transition probability: 𝐴 = 𝑃𝑡𝑟𝑎𝑛𝑠 𝑆𝑖 ቚ𝑆𝑗

∀ i, j ∈ 1, 𝑛 }; for example, the relationship between J's moods, like how today's

mood affects tomorrow's mood.


Emission probability : 𝐵 = 𝑃𝑜𝑏𝑣 𝑅𝑘 ቚ𝑆𝑗

∀ j ∈ 1, 𝑛 , k ∈ 1, 𝑚 }; for example, the relationship between J's mood and his

recreational activities for the day, like how his mood influences his activities.
⚫

An HMM can be described by a five-tuple 𝜆 = (𝐴, 𝐵, 𝜋, 𝑅, 𝑆) based on these five elements and can also be
abbreviated as 𝜆 = (𝐴, 𝐵, 𝜋).

model are unknown and need to be learned from observable data.
