HMM Learning Algorithm - Baum-Welch
⚫

Given an observation sequence without a state sequence, find the HMM.

⚫

This algorithm is essentially an EM algorithm, solving the problem: given observed values 𝑋
with a hidden variable 𝑍, find the joint probability under the HMM parameters 𝜆: 𝑃(𝑋, 𝑍|𝜆).

⚫

Solution steps:

82



Determine the log-likelihood function for the complete data.



መ .
E-step of the EM algorithm: Compute the 𝑄 function 𝑄(𝜆, 𝜆)



M-step of the EM algorithm: Maximize the 𝑄 function to find the parameters.

HMM Decoding Algorithm - Exhaustive Method
⚫

Let us assume the probable hidden state sequence generating the observation sequence is 𝑄 :


⚫

⚫

𝑄 = 𝑞1 ，𝑞2 ，𝑞3 ，𝑞4 ， … … , 𝑞𝑇 , where 𝑇 represents the sequence length, 𝑞𝑖 represents the
observed state at the 𝑖-th position, 𝑞𝑖 ∈ S.

The concept of the exhaustive method is quite straightforward:


Enumerate all the probabilities of the hidden state sequence 𝑄



Calculate the probability that each hidden state sequence produces the observed sequence 𝑃(𝑂, 𝑄)



𝑄𝑚𝑎𝑥 = 𝑎𝑟𝑔𝑚𝑎𝑥𝑄 𝑃(𝑂, 𝑄)

HMM Decoding Algorithm - Viterbi (1)
⚫

⚫

Generate 𝑄𝑚𝑎𝑥 = 𝑞1 ，𝑞2 ，𝑞3 ，𝑞4 ， … … , 𝑞𝑇 of the observation sequence 𝑂 = [𝑜1 ，𝑜2 ，𝑜3 ，𝑜4 ，
… … , 𝑜𝑇 ]. Generate 𝑄max _𝑡 = 𝑞1 ，𝑞2 ，𝑞3 ，𝑞4 ， … … , 𝑞𝑡 of the observation sequence 𝑂𝑡 = [𝑜1 ，
𝑜2 ，𝑜3 ，𝑜4 ， … … , 𝑜𝑡 ].


𝑂𝑡 is a subsequence of the first 𝑡 elements of 𝑂.



𝑄max _𝑡 is a subsequence of the first 𝑡 elements of 𝑄𝑚𝑎𝑥 .

Concept:




Forward traversal: For each hidden state at each time point in the sequence, record two pieces of information:
◼

1. The previous hidden state of the highest probability path leading to the current state.

◼

2. The highest probability of generating the observed sequence up to the current state.

Backward traceback:
◼

85

For each time point, extract the most probable sequence of hidden states from the recorded information.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

HMM Decoding Algorithm - Viterbi (2)
⚫

Assume the probable hidden state sequence generating the observation sequence is 𝑄:


𝑄 = 𝑞1 ，𝑞2 ，𝑞3 ，𝑞4 ， … … , 𝑞𝑇 , where 𝑇 represents the sequence length, 𝑞𝑖 represents the observed state at
the 𝑖-th position, 𝑞𝑖 ∈ S.

⚫

Definitions:


Assume 𝑂𝑡 = 𝑜1 ，𝑜2 ，𝑜3 ，𝑜4 ， … … , 𝑜𝑡



P(𝑂𝑡 , 𝑞t = 𝑆𝑖 ) indicates the maximum probability that the 𝑡-th hidden state is 𝑆𝑖 and produces 𝑂𝑡 .



P(𝑂𝑡 , 𝑞t = 𝑆𝑖 ) has the following properties:
◼

HMM Decoding Algorithm - Viterbi (3)
⚫

The Viterbi algorithm consists of two phases: forward computation and backward traceback:


Forward computation: Traverse the sequence points 𝑡 ∈ 1, 𝑇 :
◼

◼

At 𝑡 > 1, for each hidden state 𝑆𝑖 ,
− Record 𝑃𝑟𝑒_𝑆(𝑡, 𝑆𝑖 ) = 𝑎𝑟𝑔𝑚𝑎𝑥𝑆j P(𝑂𝑡−1 , 𝑞t−1 = 𝑆𝑗 ∗ 𝑃𝑡𝑟𝑎𝑛𝑠 𝑆𝑖 ቚ𝑆𝑗 )
− Calculate P(𝑂𝑡 , 𝑞t = 𝑆𝑖 ) = P(𝑂𝑡−1 , 𝑞t−1 = 𝑆𝑗 ) ∗ 𝑃𝑡𝑟𝑎𝑛𝑠 𝑃𝑟𝑒_𝑆(𝑡, 𝑆𝑖 ) = ቚ𝑆𝑗 ∗ 𝑃𝑜𝑏𝑣 𝑜𝑡−1 ห𝑆𝑖



◼

− At 𝑡 = T, 𝑞𝑡 = 𝑎𝑟𝑔𝑚𝑎𝑥𝑆j P(𝑂𝑇 , 𝑞𝑇 = 𝑆𝑗

GMM-HMM Speech Recognition Process
⚫

Obtain a speech WAV file. The following is a complete word recognition process:


Split the waveform into equally long frames, and extract features (MFCC) for each frame.



Run GMM on the features of each frame to obtain the probability state of each frame belonging to each hidden state.



Calculate the probability of each state sequence generating each frame based on the HMM state transition probability 𝛼 for
each word.



The word with the highest HMM sequence probability is determined to be the recognized word for the speech segment.

Disadvantages of Traditional Speech Recognition Algorithms
⚫

The main disadvantages of GMM-HMM are as follows:


In GMM-HMM, each hidden state correlates to a GMM model, which means when performing continuous word
recognition, the number of states is substantial. This leads to significant time consumption and large parameter
space during model training.



When HMM models the speech recognition problem, it heavily relies on the Markov property, implying that the

next hidden state only relates to the current state, without consideration of past and future states. In many realworld scenarios, multiple previous and future states influence a central state.


Each module is optimized and trained independently, resulting in inter-module coupling and dependency. This
prevents end-to-end task processing and optimizations geared to specific tasks.

95

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Deep Learning Speech Recognition Algorithm - Hybrid Model
⚫

Hybrid model: This approach utilizes deep neural networks to replace the GMM model in traditional GMM-HMM
frameworks. Applicable neural networks can include DNN, CNN, LSTM, and other variant structures.


Characteristics: The hybrid model uses deep neural network structures to enhance and refine the representation of speech
signal features, previously handled by GMMs.



Disadvantages: This model cannot fully detach from HMMs, as it still relies on the HMM framework. Also, the alignment of data
(sample labeling) still depends on pre-trained traditional GMM-HMM models, serving as a starting point. Essentially, it still
requires traditional GMM-HMM models and primarily aims to train acoustic models rather than provide end-to-end processing.



97

Common model structures: Several neural network models have been developed based on this concept, including:
◼

DNN+HMM

◼

CNN+HMM

◼

LSTM+HMM

◼

CLDNN+HMM

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

DNN-HMM
⚫

In this model, HMM is used to model acoustic signals, but the emission probability for each state is estimated using
DNN instead of the traditional GMM. The output of each DNN unit represents the posterior probability of states.

DNN-HMM Training Process
⚫

Initially, train the GMM-HMM model using sample data.

⚫

Using the trained GMM-HMM model, employ decoding algorithms to infer the most likely hidden state
sequences from the input audio feature sequences.

⚫

Utilize the feature-hidden state relationships obtained in step two as training samples to train the DNN

network. The input to the DNN network consists of audio features, and the output is the probability of
belonging to each hidden state.
⚫

For the input audio sequence, use the trained DNN and HMM to perform decoding and search processes
to obtain the final output text sequence.

RNN
⚫

Recurrent Neural Networks (RNNs) are a type of neural network that capture dynamic information in sequential data
through periodic connections of hidden layer nodes, allowing for the classification of sequential data.


RNNs can maintain a contextual state, and even store, learn, and express related information within arbitrarily long context
windows, allowing for extension over time sequences. Intuitively, this means there are edges between nodes of the hidden
layer at the current time and the hidden layer at the next time.

All RNNs have a chain-like structure of repeating neural network modules.
In a standard RNN, the repeating module has a very simple structure, such as a tanh layer.

BPTT
⚫

After unfolding the RNN, forward propagation sequentially calculates in time order, while BPTT
backpropagates the accumulated residuals from the final time step. This is similar in essence to training
traditional neural networks; BPTT's main difference is that it accumulates gradients at each time step.

⚫

Errors in gradients for parameters U, V, and W are calculated, and gradient descent is used to learn
optimal parameters. These gradients are computed using the chain rule of differentiation.

RNN Gradients Vanishing and Exploding
⚫

During backpropagation, RNNs push gradients backward through the sequence to the
beginning.

⚫

Gradient vanishing or exploding relates to path length, where earlier weights become fixed and
untrainable.

105

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

LSTM Networks
⚫

LSTM networks are a type of recurrent neural network designed to process and predict data
with long intervals and delays in time series.

⚫

LSTM differs from RNN by incorporating a "processor" that determines the importance of
information, known as a cell.


Each cell contains three gates: input gate, forget gate, and output gate.



Information entering the LSTM network is judged according to rules: only validated information is
retained, while irrelevant information is discarded through the forget gate.

106

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

LSTM and Speech Recognition
⚫

In recent years, the application of DNN on HMM has significantly improved the performance of speech recognition
systems. DNNs concatenate each frame of speech with adjacent frames as input to leverage context information in
the speech sequence. The number of frames input into the DNN is fixed, and different window lengths affect the
final recognition result.

⚫

RNNs, through recursion, extract context-related information in sequences, partially overcoming DNN's

shortcomings. However, RNNs are prone to gradient vanishing issues during training, hindering the memory of longterm information.
⚫

LSTM, with its specific gating units, allows error retention at current time steps and selective transmission to specific
units, thereby mitigating gradient vanishing problems.

Core Concepts of LSTM: Initial State
⚫

The key to LSTM is the cell state, represented as a horizontal line running across the top of the
diagram. The cell state acts like a conveyor belt, running through the entire chain with minimal
linear interactions, preserving information easily.

Core Concepts of LSTM: Forget Gate
⚫

The first step in LSTM is deciding which information to discard from the cell state.

⚫

This decision is made by a "forget gate", which reads ℎ𝑡−1 and 𝑥𝑡 , and outputs a value between
0 and 1 for each number in the cell state 𝐶𝑡−1 . A value of 1 means "keep completely", while 0
means "discard completely".

Core Concepts of LSTM: Input Gate
⚫

This step determines what new information to store in the cell state.

⚫

It involves two parts: An "input gate layer" (sigmoid layer) that decides which values to update. A tanh
layer that creates new candidate values to be added to the state.

Core Concepts of LSTM: Output Gate

through a tanh layer (producing values between –1 and 1) and multiplied by the sigmoid gate's output,
resulting in the specific part of the state being output.

BiRNN
⚫

The basic idea of bidirectional RNNs (BiRNNs) is that for each training sequence, there are two RNNs (like RNNs,
LSTMs, etc.) running forward and backward, respectively, and both are connected to an output layer. At each time
step t, input is provided to both RNNs in opposite directions, and the output is determined by the state of these two
single-directional RNNs combined.

Speech Data Alignment (1)
⚫

In speech datasets, it is challenging to align audio files with output text.

⚫

In traditional speech recognition models, text and audio must be strictly aligned before training the speech model.
This approach has two main drawbacks:

⚫



Strict alignment requires significant human effort and time.



After strict alignment, the model's predicted labels are only partial classifications and do not provide the entire sequence
output. Post-processing is often necessary to achieve the desired results.

The CTC loss function models the many-to-many sequence problem without alignment information.

https://distill.pub/2017/ctc/

117

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Speech Data Alignment (2)
⚫

As shown in the left diagram, the simplest solution in data alignment is to merge consecutive repeating letters.
However, words like "hello" get mapped to "helo".

⚫

The CTC loss function is an alignment-free algorithm. During data alignment, a blank character 𝜖 is introduced to
represent pauses in speech. The sequence 𝑋 is mapped to 𝑌 through ℬ. The ℬ operation includes:


Merging consecutive identical symbols



Removing blank characters

https://distill.pub/2017/ctc/
118

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

CTC Loss Function
⚫

CTC implements variable length mapping. This alignment method has the following characteristics:


Time slice mapping between X and Y is monotonic, meaning if X moves forward one time slice, Y either stays still or also moves
forward one time slice.



The mapping between X and Y is many-to-one, meaning multiple outputs may correspond to one mapping, but not vice versa.
Therefore, the length of X is greater than or equal to the length of Y.

𝑐

RNN + CTC
⚫

The input is an audio feature sequence, and the output is a letter sequence.


The length of the output letter sequence matches the length of the input audio
feature sequence.



One challenge in using this model is how to evaluate the difference between the
model's output letter sequence and the target letter sequence. This is because

the length of the audio feature sequence is much longer than the target letter
sequence, resulting in a longer output letter sequence that cannot be aligned
with the target sequence.


The CTC loss function is used for evaluation.

It evaluates the difference between the output letter sequence and the target letter
sequence of inconsistent lengths.

120

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• For more details, see the paper: Graves A, Jaitly N. "Towards end-to-end speech
recognition with recurrent neural networks." International Conference on Machine
Learning, 2014: 1764–1772.
• CTC loss function stands for connectionist temporal classification, and the detailed
calculation process is described in the paper: Graves A. "Supervised sequence labelling
with recurrent neural networks." 2012 [J]. URL: http://books.google.com/books, 2012.

RNN + CTC Process
⚫

The overall process of using this model for speech recognition is as follows:


Training process: Use training sample data and the CTC loss function to train the model based on the
model structure.



Prediction process: For the input audio feature sequence, get the corresponding letter sequence after

passing through the network, and use beam search to find the optimal path.

121

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• For more details, see the paper: Graves A, Jaitly N. "Towards end-to-end speech
recognition with recurrent neural networks." International Conference on Machine
Learning, 2014: 1764–1772.

End2End Model
⚫

The End2End model refers to a model where the input is a sequence of speech features and the output is
directly a sequence of letters or more coarse-grained (word) sequences.


Advantages: End-to-end processing of speech recognition problems, without the need for numerous
intermediate steps.



Challenges: Training the network without labeled data using forced input-output alignment. Currently, there are
two methods:
◼

Using RNN series networks, relying on the CTC loss function to evaluate the difference between the obtained sequence
and the target sequence.

◼

Using Seq2Seq network structure for automatic alignment, using the cross-entropy loss function to evaluate the difference
between the predicted sequence and the target sequence.



123

Common network models include:
◼

CNN/RNN/LSTM+CTC

◼

Seq2Seq+CE, Seq2Seq+Attention+CE

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Seq2Seq
⚫

A sequence to sequence (Seq2Seq) model is composed of two parts: encoder and decoder, typically
implemented using RNN/LSTM/GRU networks. Seq2Seq's input is a variable-length sequence, and the
output is also a variable-length sequence.

⚫

Roles of encoder and decoder:


The encoder converts the variable-length input

Y1

Y2

Y3

sequence into a fixed-length context vector,
encoding the information of the input sequence



The decoder decodes the context vector,

Semantic
code c

Encoder

in this context vector.
x1

x2

x3

Decoder

x4

converting it into a variable-length output
sequence.

Encoder-decoder framework
124

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The full name of Seq2Seq is sequence to sequence. The basic Seq2Seq = encoder +
decoder + semantic code c (an intermediate state vector connecting the two, which can
be understood as the regularity of the connection between the two languages). In the
encoder, the variable-length signal sequence is transformed into a fixed-length vector
representation, essentially feature compression; the decoder converts this fixed-length
vector into a variable-length target signal sequence. The encoder and decoder can be of
the same structure (CNN, RNN, Transformer) or different structures.
• For example, one could be RNN and the other CNN (e.g., Image Caption).

Seq2Seq in Speech Recognition
⚫

The model takes an audio feature sequence as input and outputs a letter sequence.

⚫

Using the Seq2Seq model, the lengths of the input and output sequences do not need to be the same. Therefore,
the input can be an audio feature sequence, and the output can be a letter sequence or a word sequence with a
larger granularity.

⚫

To evaluate the difference between the model's output letter sequence and the target letter sequence, we can
directly use the cross-entropy loss function.

125

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• For detailed reference, see the article: Bahdanau D, Chorowski J, Serdyuk D, et al. Endto-end attention-based large vocabulary speech recognition[C]//2016 IEEE International
Conference on Acoustics, Speech and Signal Processing (ICASSP). IEEE, 2016: 4945–4949.

Problems and Optimization of Seq2Seq Model
⚫

The Seq2Seq model performs poorly when dealing with overly long sequence data due to two
main reasons:

⚫



The inherent long-term dependency issue of RNN models (which can be solved with LSTM/GRU).



The context vector cannot fully represent the information of the entire input sequence.

When decoding, the decoder needs to consider the entire sequence, which can introduce a lot
of irrelevant noise or information, leading to information overload. In fact, most outputs are
related to parts of the input sequence rather than the entire sequence. In this case, the
attention mechanism is introduced based on the Seq2Seq model.

126

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Attention Mechanism
⚫

The attention mechanism focuses on specific parts of the source sequence using a direct connection with the
encoder at each step of the decoder.

⚫

The attention mechanism focuses on more critical information in the input, reducing attention to other information,
and even filtering out irrelevant information. This can solve the information overload problem and improve the
efficiency and accuracy of task processing.

• Adding the attention mechanism to the encoder-decoder framework: The context vector
encoded by the encoder is weighted with each output during the decoding process. The
weights are adjusted to get different context vectors for each decoding step.

What Is Natural Language?
Natural Language

⚫



It is a system of symbols which form words and grammar, with speech as the audial representation.
Text and sound are two attributes of a language.



Natural language is a tool for human communication and transmitting thoughts. The knowledge
recorded and transmitted in the form of language throughout the human history accounts for more
than 80% of total human knowledge.



6

It is the default and distinct from human-made languages such as Java and C++.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

What Is NLP? (1)
NLP

⚫



It is a technology that uses computers to process and analyze various types of information relating to
written and spoken languages that are unique to humans. ---- Feng Zhiwei



NLP can be defined as the study of language issues in human-to-human and human-to-computer
communication. NLP needs to develop models that represent language capabilities and language
applications, establish computing frameworks to implement such language models, propose
corresponding methods to continuously improve language models, design various practical systems
based on language models, and discuss the evaluation technologies of these practical systems. ----Bill

Manaris

7

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• NLP mainly includes two parts: natural language understanding and natural language
generation, which are supported by various basic algorithms.
▫ Natural language understanding (NLU): enables computers to understand natural
languages (human languages). Specifically, it is to understand languages and texts
and extract useful information for downstream tasks. Examples include emotion
recognition, intent recognition, information retrieval (including personalized search,
semantic search, and text matching), and information extraction (named entity
extraction, relationship extraction, and event extraction).
▫ Natural language generation (NLG): provides structured data, texts, charts, audio,
and videos to generate text that can be understood by human beings. NLG can be
further classified into three types: text-to-text, such as translation and abstraction;
text-to-other, such as text-to-image; and other-to-text, such as video-to-text.

Importance of NLP
Before AI emerged, machines intelligently processed structured data, such as spreadsheets.

⚫

However, most data in life is unstructured. For example, articles, images, audio, and videos.
There is a vast amount of textual data and information. To enable machines to help us handle

⚫

problems, we need to analyze and utilize the data to empower machines to comprehend our
language, thus establishing a communication bridge between humans and machines.

NLU Levels
⚫

Natural language understanding and analysis is a hierarchical process, which can be divided into the following five levels:


Speech analysis. This distinguishes independent phonemes from a speech stream according to a phoneme form rule, and then
finds corresponding syllables, lexemes or words according to the rule.



Lexical analysis. This finds the lexemes of a word and obtains linguistic information from them.



Syntax analysis. This is analysis of the structure of sentences and phrases to find out the relationship between them and their
function in sentences.



Semantic analysis. This finds the definition of words, their structural meaning, and their combined meaning, so as to determine
the true concept expressed by a language.



Pragmatic analysis. This is the study of the influence of the external environment on the users’ language.

Speech analysis

Difficulties in NLP (1)
⚫

Lexical ambiguity:




Word segmentation: It is difficult to determine the segmentation boundary of words.
◼

the /New York/-New /Haven /Railroad

◼

the /New /York-New /Haven /Railroad

A word has multiple meanings.
◼



Never trouble troubles until troubles trouble you

Named entity recognition: It is difficult to recognize out-of-vocabulary words such as names, proper nouns, and
acronyms.

15

◼

Supreme: Name of person or an adjective

◼

Huaming: Name of person or organization

◼

Move: Name of organization or a verb

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Difficulties in NLP (2)
⚫

Syntax ambiguity: Dependency at the syntax level is affected by the context.


16

The chicken is ready to eat:
◼

The chicken is ready to eat, and they all look hungry.

◼

The chicken is ready to eat, so please bring out the cooked chicken.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Difficulties in NLP (3)
⚫

Semantic ambiguity


17

At last, a computer understands you like your mother.
◼

Meaning 1: A computer will understand you like your mother does.

◼

Meaning 2: The computer understands that you like your mother.

◼

Meaning 3: The computer will understand you the way it understands your mother.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Difficulties in NLP (4)
⚫

Pragmatic ambiguity


"What are you doing?"
◼

Just inquiry: Simple inquiries between friends, wanting to know what you are doing.

◼

Anger questioning: When the mother says it to the mischievous son, the actual meaning is that the son
might have done some bad things.

◼

18

Doubt: You did something inappropriate or in secret. This has the meaning of investigation or questioning.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Development History of NLP

Deep learningassisted
Statistics-based
method
Rule-based method
Rationalist approach
Empiricist approach

Turing test

19

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Rule-based method: This approach has unavoidable drawbacks. Firstly, rules cannot be
applied to all statements. Secondly, this method requires that developers must be
proficient in both computer science and linguistics. Therefore, although this method
addresses some simple issues, it fails to make natural language understanding practical.
• Statistics-based method: The rapid development of the Internet gives plentiful accessible
content, and hardware is continuously updated and improved. The NLP approach is
transitioning from empiricism to rationalism, with the statistics-based method gradually
replacing the rule-based method.
• Deep learning-assisted: end-to-end training from input to output. Prepare the input and
output data pair. Then, design and train a neural network to perform the expected task.
Recurrent Neural Network (RNN) is one of the most commonly used methods for NLP.
Models such as GRU and LSTM have triggered rounds of upsurge.

How Are Words Represented? - Discrete Symbol Representation
⚫

One-hot encoding is a method of representing word vectors by using discrete symbols. The length of a
vector equals to the total number of words in the vocabulary.
Index position of each word in the vocabulary

Vocabulary: This is a simple example

This = [1, 0, 0, 0, 0]
is = [0, 1, 0, 0, 0]
a = [0, 0, 1, 0, 0]
simple = [0, 0, 0, 1, 0]
example = [0, 0, 0, 0, 1]
Vocabulary size

⚫

Question: What are the disadvantages of one-hot encoding?

27

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

How Are Words Represented? - Distributional Semantic
Representation
⚫

Distributional semantic representation: Each word is no longer a completely orthogonal 0-1 vector, but a point in a
multi-dimensional space, which is represented as a real number vector. In many cases, this distributional
representation is also called “word embedding”.

⚫

Distributional hypothesis: The meaning of a word can be inferred from the context in which it appears.

... New York traffic police just released the news ...
...The reporter learned from the New York government that...
...For me, giving up my job in New York is tantamount to taking myself...

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Distributional semantic representation addresses the problem that one-hot vectors cannot
represent semantic similarities between words.
• The true meaning of a word should be determined by its context.

Applying Singular Value Decomposition (SVD) to a Co-occurrence Matrix
⚫

𝑋 is a co-occurrence matrix. It is decomposed by Singular Value Decomposition (SVD) into a lowdimensional, dense matrix.

⚫

Question: What are the disadvantages of applying SVD to a co-occurrence matrix?

31

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The co-occurrence matrix is high-dimensional and sparse.
• The co-occurrence matrix disregards word sequence.
• Each time a word is added, the co-occurrence matrix needs to be recalculated.
• SVD learns only shallow semantics.

Why Don't We Learn the Distributional Representation of Words

Applying SVD to a co-occurrence matrix is a way to directly calculate word vectors based on

statistical data. However, it is not a unique, optimal method.

FastText
⚫

FastText is a text representation method based on the BoW model. It decomposes words into
subwords and adds the vector representations of the subwords to obtain word vectors, fully
utilizing character N-gram information.

Feature Extraction: Bag of Words
⚫

Bag of Words (BoW) is a simple text vectorization method. It disregards the order of words in a
sentence and focuses only on the number of occurrences of words in the sentence of a
vocabulary.

Feature Selection
⚫

Features obtained using BoW or TF-IDF are typically high-dimensional and sparse, resulting in
poor training performance for classifiers. High-dimensional data also affects training and
prediction speeds. Therefore, feature selection is often employed to eliminate redundant

features. Common feature selection methods in text classification are as follows:

49



Chi-square test



Mutual information



Information gain



...

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Chi-square Test
⚫

The chi-square test originates from chi-square statistics. The test compares each class and word
in the contingency table to see if they are related, and measures the lack of independence
between them (feature and class). A large value for chi-square indicates a low independence

and high correlation.

50

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Chi-square Value Calculation

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• O is the observation, and E is the expected value.

Deep Learning Method: TextCNN
⚫

TextCNN is a model that uses convolutional neural networks (CNNs) to classify text.

⚫

Text is sent to the neural network after word embedding. Unlike the CNN, the convolutional operation of TextCNN is used on onedimensional data.

⚫

Similar to the N-gram model, the features extracted by TextCNN are local relationships between words.

Wait
for
the
video
and

rant

n x k representation of
sentence with static and
non-static channels
55

Convolutional laver with

Max-over-time
pooling

Fully connected layer with

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Reference link: https://arxiv.org/abs/1408.5882
• When we brought CNN forward, it was generally considered that CNN belongs to the
computer vision (CV) field. However, in 2014, Yoon Kim made some transformations on the
input layer of CNN and proposed the text classification model TextCNN. Compared with the
traditional CNN for images, TextCNN has no change in the network structure (even
simpler). As shown in the figure, the TextCNN has only one convolutional layer and one
max-pooling layer. The output is connected to the external softmax for n classification.
• The biggest difference between CNN for images and TextCNN lies in the input data. The
image is two-dimensional data, and features are extracted by sliding the convolution kernel
of the image from left to right and from top to bottom. The natural language is onedimensional data. Although a two-dimensional vector is generated through wordembedding, it is meaningless to perform convolution by sliding the word vector from left to
right. For example, if the word "today" corresponds to the vector [0, 0, 0, 0, 1], you can
obtain vectors [0,0], [0,0], [0,0], and [0,1] by sliding from left to right based on the window
size of 1 x 2, but all the four vectors correspond to the word "today". Such sliding is not
helpful.

• Generally, the hidden status of the forward/backward LSTM in the last time step is used for
concatenation. After passing through a softmax layer (the output layer uses the softmax
activation function), a multi-class classification is performed. Alternatively, you can obtain
the hidden state of the forward/backward LSTM at each time step, concatenate the two
hidden states at each time step, obtain the average value of the concatenated hidden
states at all time steps, pass through a softmax layer (the output layer uses the softmax
activation function), and perform a multi-class classification (use the sigmoid activation
function for 2-class classification).

Hidden Markov Model (HMM)
⚫

HMM has two assumptions:


Hidden state independence assumption (Homogeneous Markov independence assumption): The
current state is related only to the previous state.



Observation independence assumption: The current observation is generated only by the current
hidden state, and is independent from other observations.
ORG

O

Huawei

is

O

O

O

LOC

Hidden
states

Observa

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

a technology company located in Shenzhen, China.

Label Bias Problem in HMM
⚫

The Markov assumption of HMM allows for partial normalization of transition probabilities
when calculating the label transition probability. This results in states with fewer transitions
having a higher probability than those with more transitions. This causes a preference for states

with fewer transitions.

0.5

0.3
0.3

0.5

65

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

0.4

Context Problem in HMM
⚫

The output independence assumption allows the probability at the current time step of the
algorithm to depend only on the current observation and does not account for context, which
severely limits the performance of HMM.

66

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Conditional Random Field (CRF)
⚫

CRF cancels the two assumptions of HMM, and regards both label transition and context input
as global features. It also performs global probability normalization, resolving HMM’s problems
of label bias and missing context.

• Because the output of BiLSTM for each word is label scores, we can select the label with the

training data.

Language Model and Text Generation
What is a language model?

⚫



It predicts what is the next most likely word of the given word sequences.
You?
I love
working?

NLP?


A formal definition: Given the word sequence 𝑤1 , 𝑤2 , … , 𝑤𝑖−1 ， , it calculates the probability distribution of the next
word 𝑤𝑖 .

𝑃 𝑤𝑖 𝑤1 , 𝑤2 , … , 𝑤𝑖−1


， where 𝑤𝑖 could be any word in the vocabulary.

Language models are also used to perform probability computation on segments of text:
𝑃 𝑤1 , 𝑤2 , … , 𝑤𝑚 = 𝑃 𝑤1 𝑃 𝑤2 𝑤1 … 𝑃(𝑤𝑖 |𝑤1 , 𝑤2 , … , 𝑤𝑖−1 ) … 𝑃(𝑤𝑚 |𝑤1 , 𝑤2 , … , 𝑤𝑚−1 )

71

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

N-Gram Language Model
⚫

The n-gram model estimates conditional probability and ignores the impact of preceding words
whose distance is equal to or greater than n. Therefore, if the frequency count is used to
compute the conditional probability, the following formula can be used:

ELMo Word Vector
⚫

After pre-training a bidirectional model, the encoding part can calculate the dynamic word
vector representation of any text. In the ELMo model, multiple hidden layer vectors contain
various layers and granularities of text information.


An LSTM hidden layer, closer to the top layer, generally encodes more semantic information. This is
relevant for tasks with high reading comprehension requirements for semantic information.



Hidden layers near the bottom focus more on lexical and syntactic information, making them suitable
for named entity recognition tasks.

Sequence-to-Sequence (Seq2Seq)
⚫

Seq2Seq consists of an encoder and a decoder network, and it is typically implemented using
RNN/LSTM/GRU networks. Both the input and output of Seq2Seq are non-fixed-length
sequences.

⚫

The functions of the encoder and decoder are as follows:


Y1

Y2

Y3

The encoder encodes the non-fixed-length
Semantic
code c

Encoder

input sequence information into a fixed-

Decoder

length context vector.


The decoder decodes the context vector,

x1

x2

x3

x4

converting it into a non-fixed-length output
sequence.

80

Encoder-decoder framework

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• A basic Seq2Seq consists of an encoder, a decoder, and the semantic code c (an
intermediate state vector connecting the two, which can be understood as the principle of
the connection between the two languages). In the encoder, the variable-length signal
sequence is transformed into a fixed-length vector representation, essentially feature
compression; the decoder converts this fixed-length vector into a variable-length target
signal sequence. The encoder and decoder can be of the same structure (CNN, RNN,
Transformer) or different structures.
• For example, one could be RNN and the other CNN (e.g., Image Caption).

Transformers: Attention is All You Need (1)
⚫

Transformers are a novel model based on the Seq2Seq structure proposed by Google
researchers. The method has quickly swept across the field of NLP.

⚫

Unlike conventional models such as a recurrent neural network (RNN), transformers use the
self-attention mechanism, along with a standard feedforward neural network. Transformers do
not depend on any recurrent unit, or convolution operation. The self-attention mechanism can
model the relationship between any two units in a sequence to better capture long-distance
dependencies.

⚫

Because transformers can also be used as a representation model, they are widely used in
other NLP fields. Currently, the popular pre-training model BERT is based on a transformer.

81

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Transformers: Attention is All You Need (2)

• In addition to the attention mechanism between encoders and decoders, transformers
introduce a self-attention mechanism within encoders and decoders to better capture
context semantics. This is more effective than traditional RNN-based encoders and
decoders, which can only process information sequentially, and have lower efficiency. In
contrast, the self-attention mechanism allows for parallel processing, fully utilizing
hardware resources for acceleration.

Transformer Architecture
⚫

A transformer consists of an encoder and a decoder.

⚫

Decoder

⚫

https://arxiv.org/pdf/1706.03762
84

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Components in the Encoder Block (1)
⚫

The modules contained within an encoder or decoder of a transformer are similar:


Input embedding: Converts input data (such as words or tags in text) into numerical vectors
processable by model.



Positional encoding: Captures the sequence and positional relationship between inputs.



Multi-head attention: Is composed of multiple attention sub-layers, and used to enhance the model's
ability to focus on various positions.
◼

Self-attention: Is used to learn associations with various positions, capturing more comprehensive contextual
information.



Feedforward: A fully connected feedforward neural network is used to further transform an input
vector sequence.

85

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• These operations form a transformer layer. The execution sequence of each module is: SelfAttention → Residual Connection → Layer Normalization → Feedforward Network →
Residual Connection → Layer Normalization. An encoder may include multiple such layers.
For instance, a six-layer encoder can be built, with each layer performing these operations.
The result at the top layer serves as the final encoding result and is transmitted to the
decoder.

Components in the Encoder Block (2)


Residual connection (marked as "Add"): For both the self-attention and linear sublayers, there is an
additional, direct connection from an input to an output. It is a cross-sublayer direct connection. The
residual connection can improve the transmission efficiency of deep network information.



Layer normalization (marked as "Norm"): Layer normalization is performed on an output vector to
normalize a result vector value range. This is done before the self-attention and linear sublayers
achieve final output to facilitate subsequent processing.

86

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• These operations form a transformer layer. The execution sequence of each module is: SelfAttention → Residual Connection → Layer Normalization → Feedforward Network →
Residual Connection → Layer Normalization. An encoder may include multiple such layers.
For instance, a six-layer encoder can be built, with each layer performing these operations.
The result at the top layer serves as the final encoding result and is transmitted to the
decoder.

Positional Encoding in a Transformer
⚫

Transformers employ trigonometric function positional encoding (absolute positional encoding).
𝑃𝐸(𝑝𝑜𝑠,2𝑖) = sin(𝑝𝑜𝑠/100002𝑖/𝑑𝑚𝑜𝑑𝑒𝑙 )
𝑃𝐸(𝑝𝑜𝑠,2𝑖+1) = cos(𝑝𝑜𝑠/100002𝑖/𝑑𝑚𝑜𝑑𝑒𝑙 )
pos represents the position of a word in a sentence, d represents the dimension of PE (same as
word embedding), 2i represents an even dimension, and 2i+1 represents an odd dimension (2i ≤ d
and 2i+1 ≤ d).


Why sin and cos: For each position i and dimension d, sine and cosine functions are used to alternately generate
the position codes, where the wavelengths form a geometric progression. This encoding method is related to the
absolute values of each position in the sequence. Due to the properties of trigonometric functions, the method

allows the vector of a position a+b to be represented by the combination of vectors for positions a and b,
enabling the expression of relative position information. For the spacing k with a fixed length, PE(pos+k) can be
calculated using PE(pos).

88

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Compared to conventional learnable position embedding, trigonometric function positional
coding does not require additional training parameters. Positional coding uses a fixed
mathematical formula to directly calculate the result, which reduces the number of
parameters in a model.
• Because the trigonometric function positional coding has an explicit generation rule, the
model can be more easily extended to unseen sequence lengths.
• The trigonometric function positional encoding can also express relative position
information to some extent. By calculating the difference or proportion between different
position codes, the model can infer the relative position relationship between entities.
However, in an actual use process, the hidden relative position information expression
model cannot always be learned.

requires only one matrix (consisting of the representation vector of each word). So we need
a way to compress these eight matrices into one. What should we do?

⚫

The BERT model architecture utilizes a multi-layer bidirectional transformer encoder to implement deep
bidirectional pre-training. All layers are pre-trained based on the context. Compared with the unidirectional
language model, BERT model training has a larger volume of information, and has a more accurate

Self-supervised Learning
⚫

Take a large amount of unlabeled data x. Divide it into two parts: input x' and label x". Then,
train the model so that the output y is as close as possible to the label x''. Note that the label x''
is not added by humans. It already exists in the data.

Supervised
⚫

Self-supervised

BERT is trained through self-supervised learning. During training, BERT learns from a large

unlabeled corpus to predict the probability distribution of the next word in the given context.

Pre-Training and Fine-Tuning
⚫

BERT includes two stages: pre-training and fine-tuning. In the pre-training stage, the model is trained on unlabeled
data. In the fine-tuning stage, the pre-trained BERT model is used to fine-tune model parameters based on the
labeled data from downstream tasks. The BERT model is first initialized with the pre-trained parameters. Then, all
parameters are trained with the labeled data from downstream tasks.

https://arxiv.org/pdf/1
810.04805

97

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Masked Language Model (MLM)
⚫

BERT is a multi-task model. Its pre-training task consists of two self-supervised tasks: MLM and next
sentence prediction (NSP).

⚫

MLM is the process of masking some words from the input corpus during training and predicting these

masked words based on the context.


There is an 80% probability that tokens are replaced with [Mask]. For example, the sentence "my dog is cute" is
replaced with "my dog is [Mask]".



There is a 10% probability that tokens are replaced with other words. For example, the word "cute" is replaced
with another word, "apple". This transforms the original sentence "my dog is cute" to "my dog is apple".



There is a 10% probability that the original token is retained. For example, the sentence "my dog is cute" remains
unchanged.

98

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

NSP (1)
⚫

NSP is used to determine if sentence B follows sentence A.

⚫

Many important downstream tasks, such as question answering (QA) and natural language
inference (NLI), are based on understanding the relationship between two sentences, which
cannot be directly captured by language modeling. To train a model to understand sentence
relationships, BERT employs the following NSP strategy:


⚫

If sentence B follows sentence A, the output is IsNext. If not, the output is NotNext.

The training data is generated by randomly selecting two consecutive sentences from the

parallel corpus. There is a 50% probability that two sentences have an IsNext relationship.
There is a 50% probability that sentence B is randomly selected from the corpus, meaning the
output is NotNext. The relationship is saved in [CLS].
99

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

LIama Structure
⚫

LIama is a large language model released by Meta AI, using the
decoder-only architecture with multiple versions, including 7B, 13B,
33B, and 60B. It is trained on the public dataset (with 1.4 TB tokens).

The model structure details of the 7B version are as follows:

104



Consists of 32 block stacks.



Employs BPE to process text data.



Uses rotary positional encoding.



RMSNorm is used for normalization in each sub-layer.



Uses the SwiGLU activation function.

Section Summary
⚫

Word vectors: Pre-trained word vector models such as Word2Vec and Glove learn the distributed semantic
expression of a word in a corpus. This provides rich semantic features for downstream tasks.

⚫

Text classification: The first and most important step of text classification is to encode the entire text into a vector.
Traditional methods include BoW and TF-IDF. In deep learning, this step can be automatically completed through
networks such as CNN, RNN, and transformers.

⚫

Sequence labeling: Each input position has a corresponding output. Named entity recognition is a typical sequence
labeling task.

⚫

Language model and text generation: Language models are mainly used for generation tasks.

⚫

Transformers: The sequence-to-sequence network uses an encoder-decoder architecture to implement conversion
from one sequence to another. The attention mechanism can resolve the information bottleneck problem of a
traditional RNN encoder-decoder architecture. It can dynamically generate vector expressions of sentences.

Multi-Modal Convergence
Foundation models are no longer limited to a single modality, such as images, text, or speech. Instead,

⚫

they start to implement multi-modal fusion, that is, they can process and generate multiple types of
data. This will significantly improve the effect, universality, and generalization of AI models, so that the
models can capture and express complex knowledge and information more accurately.

Scale and complexity
With the enhancement of computing capabilities and algorithm progress, the scale of

⚫

foundation models may be further expanded in the future, and the model complexity will
increase to process more complex tasks and data types. Self-supervised learning is performed
based on massive data, and a unified model and paradigm are used to solve various AI tasks.

7

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Lightweight
To enable foundation models to run on resource-constrained devices, model compression and

⚫

transfer learning technologies will continue to be developed to reduce the size of models and
improve their migration capabilities.


The lightweight of foundation models uses a series of technical means to reduce model complexity
and computing resource requirements while ensuring model precision. This improves the model
loading speed, reduces memory usage, and reduces network transmission costs, making models
easier to deploy and use.

8

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Synergy of Models of All Sizes
In the future, AI systems may use foundation models and small models to work together. Small

⚫

models can be used as sample value judgment models to help foundation models quickly learn.
In addition, the capabilities of foundation models can be transferred to small models to
implement association and mutual assistance between them. This cooperative working mode
will improve the efficiency and performance of AI systems.

9

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Embodied Intelligence
⚫

Embodied Intelligence (EI) is a general-purpose agent that can understand, infer, and interact
with the physical world. The EI agent usually has a multi-modal perception and cognition
capability, can obtain external information through a plurality of senses such as vision, hearing,
and tactile, and can interact with the environment through a physical action. Such an agent can
learn and adapt to the environment in which the agent is located, perform complex tasks, and
perform intelligent behavior similar to that of a human.


EI aims to create intelligent systems that can simulate humans and other creatures to learn and adapt
to the environment in nature.

Controversies Over AI
⚫

As AI technology advances, people are gaining a better understanding of AI. However, many
worry about the future with AI.

Is our world real, or just an illusion?

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• What you see might not be real.
• Ethical concerns will be governed by strict policies and regulations.
• Partial job loss could result.
• Privacy risks exist but can be mitigated with advanced technologies like differential privacy,
model fingerprinting, and encryption.
• Controllability empowers trainees to think critically.

Seeing Is Not Believing
⚫

As computer vision advances, the trustworthiness of images and videos is declining. Now, we
can use technologies such as PS and GAN to create fake images.

⚫

Example:


Weight-loss drug sellers use Photoshop to change the body shapes of people in images and use the
fake images for diet drug ads.



Lyrebird is a tool that can clone human voices based on a few minutes of recording samples. Such a
tool could be exploited for malicious purposes.



15

GAN can generate fake room pictures for rental or hotel booking platforms.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Ethical Concerns of AI
⚫

Discrimination and stigmatization: AI may threaten
social fairness and justice, and restrict people's
freedom of choice.

⚫

Autonomous decision-making: AI's autonomous
decision-making can harm human control and lead to
untraceable, irreproducible errors that are hard to fix.

⚫

Defects: AI systems often have unclear goals, methods,
and decision-making processes.

⚫

Damage to human dignity, minds, and bodies: Robots
create unsafe environments and be used for malicious
purposes. People's privacy is at risk, making them
vulnerable to deception and manipulation.

16

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Privacy and Data Security
⚫

In the era of big data and AI, we can obtain information more conveniently and efficiently. However, while gaining
convenience, our behavior is recorded, learned, and used all the time. How do we protect our data privacy?

• 1. For users: Before obtaining user information, mobile
apps must obtain user consent (privacy clauses). Users
can reject the scope of documents required by the app for
proactive protection.

• 2. For the society: Governments need to actively promote
the formulation of privacy protection clauses, implement
basic industry rules, and strengthen supervision.
• 3. For developers: Confidential computing, model privacy
protection, federated learning, or adversarial learning can
be used to prevent reverse attacks and protect user
privacy. Alternatively, a well-established privacy
protection framework, for example, can be helpful.

17

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Reference:
• Confidential computing: Data transmission and computing are confidential, and privacy
protection is costly.
• Model privacy protection: Commonly used methods include data anonymization,
differential privacy training, model encryption, and model obfuscation. (Differential privacy
can measure and control the leakage of trained data by models.)
• Federated learning: Generally, multi-party joint machine learning is performed without
data sharing. It is essentially a distributed machine learning framework with limited data
access. Compute nodes share only gradients but not raw data.

Data Fairness and Transparency
⚫

Currently, most AI models are trained on data created by humans, and this data strongly
influences the model's output.


During data collection, processing, and application, we must ensure that all groups and individuals
are treated fairly and equally, and avoid unfairness caused by data deviation or discriminatory
algorithms.



Data transparency means that the data processing and application process should be clear and
understandable, and related information and decision-making basis should be open and transparent
so that data users and individuals affected by data can understand the data source, processing
method, and result.

18

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Impact of AI on Employment and Society
⚫

AI's advancement reshapes employment and societal norms.

19



The application of automation and intelligence technologies has replaced some traditional jobs with
machines, especially repetitive and low-skill jobs. It also creates new career needs, such as the need
for professionals to develop, maintain, and optimize these intelligent systems.



AI technologies boost production efficiency and slash costs, empowering businesses to swiftly adapt
and outcompete rivals in dynamic markets.



Social inequality is on the rise, and while AI spawns new job opportunities, it might also widen the
gap. Those who can master and apply AI technologies may have access to more economic and social
resources.



As AI technology spreads, ensuring data security and privacy protection, along with developing and
enforcing pertinent laws, presents fresh challenges to social governance.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Throughout the course of history, human beings have been seeking ways to improve
efficiency, that is, to obtain more with fewer resources. We use sharp stones to hunt and
gather food efficiently; we use steam engines to reduce the demand for horses. Every step
towards automation changes our lives. In the AI era, what tasks will be taken over by AI?

• As we all know, in the case of deep learning, the larger the dataset, the more accurate the
model. At present, supervised learning is used primarily. Therefore, data needs to be
labeled.
• When there is a large amount of data, you can use intelligent labeling to improve efficiency
while saving manpower.
• The key to ModelArts intelligent labeling is active learning algorithm, which enables
automatic data labeling, accompanied with manual correction, hugely improving labeling
efficiency.
• After a dataset is ready, you can use a data feature statistics function to evaluate the
dataset quality. ModelArts automatically extracts some features and displays them using
graphs, and also provides data optimization suggestions. For example, it can automatically
extract features from image datasets, such as bounding box quantity, bounding box size,
brightness, ambiguity, resolution, and color.

• If I know nothing about AI or coding, can I still use ModelArts to develop AI models? The
answer is yes. You can use ModelArts ExeML to do this.
• ExeML is friendly to AI beginners. Basically, you can create an AI model in three steps with
zero coding. Step 1: Upload and label data. Step 2: Have the model trained automatically.
Step 3: Deploy the model with one click.
• ExeML automatically searches for the optimal neural network architecture and

this paper, experiments are performed only on machine translation, defeating all
SOTA benchmarks of machine translation.

Transformer uses the attention mechanism. Therefore, this chapter starts with the
principle of the attention mechanism and describes the important details of
Transformer.

Why Attention Is Introduced
⚫

Attention: attention mechanism.

⚫

When we use a convolutional neural network (CNN) model to recognize an image, how can we make the model
know the importance of different local information in the image?
How do we resolve the long-distance "memory" issue when we use the recurrent neural network (RNN) model to

⚫

deal with NLP-related tasks?

5

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Right figure source: customized.
• The mechanism of visual attention is an innate ability of the human brain. When we see an
image, we take a glance of it and then focus on the key target area. For example, when we
look at the above figures, we easily focus on content such as Peking University. Imagine
that if every local information should be focused on, it will inevitably consume a lot of
energy, which is not conducive to human survival and evolution. Similarly, introducing a
similar mechanism into the deep learning network can simplify the model and accelerate
computing.
• Attention is introduced to focus on key points. Even if the text is long, you can grasp the key
points without losing important information. The colored text in the figure is the key point.

Attention Mechanism Calculation Procedure
K, Q, V:

⚫



Query (to match others): query vector, which provides
guidance.



Key (to be matched): key vector, used for matching.



Value (information to be extracted): value vector,
information itself.

Phase 1

Softmax()

Phase 2

Three-steps:

⚫



Step 1: Calculate the similarity between the query and key
to obtain the weights.



Step 2: Normalize the weights to obtain weights that can
be directly used.



6

Step 3: Perform weighted sum on the weights and value.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Phase 3

Attention in Machine Translation
Machine translation is a process of converting a natural language (source) into another natural language

⚫

(target) by using a computer.
Neural machine translation (NMT) uses the encoder-decoder architecture to implement the modeling of

⚫

variable-length input sentences. The encoder understands sentences in the source language and forms a
floating-point number vector of a specific dimension. Then, the decoder generates a translation result of
the target language word by word based on the vector.
Seq2Seq is a general-purpose encoder-decoder framework. It is often used in scenarios such as machine

⚫

translation, text abstract, chatbot, reading comprehension, speech recognition, image description

generation, and image Q&A.

7

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Seq2Seq Model
A Seq2Seq model consists of an encoder and a decoder. Generally, the RNN, LSTM, and GRU networks

⚫

are used. The input and output of a Seq2Seq model are variable-length sequences.
The functions of the encoder and decoder are as follows:

⚫



The encoder converts the input variable-length sequence into a context vector with a fixed length, and encodes
information about the input sequence in the context vector.



The decoder performs a reverse process, that is, decodes the context vector, and converts it into an output
variable-length sequence.

8

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Issues and Optimization of Seq2Seq Models
⚫

⚫

A Seq2Seq model is not suitable for processing long sequence data, because:


Long-term dependency on RNN (this can be resolved by using LSTM or GRU).



The context vector cannot represent the information of the entire input sequence.

During decoding, the decoder needs to consider all sequences, which contain many irrelevant
noises and information. As a result, information overload may occur. Most output is related to
only a part of the input sequence, but not the entire sequence. In this case, attention
mechanism is introduced to Seq2Seq models.

10

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

1.

11

Attention Mechanism


Algorithm Innovation and Engineering Optimization of DeepSeek

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Attention Mechanism
⚫

Attention mechanism: In each step of the decoder, a direct connection to the encoder is used to focus on
a specific part of the source sequence.

⚫

It focuses on more critical information in the input data and even filters out irrelevant information,

resolving the overload problem and improving the efficiency and accuracy of task processing.

encoding

hidden state. The weighted sum of encoder hidden state and attention
distribution are calculated.

Algorithm Innovation and Engineering Optimization of DeepSeek

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Birth of Transformer
⚫

In 2017, the Google machine translation team published Attention is All You Need,
which proposed Transformer and completely abandoned network structures such as
RNN and CNN. Instead, only the attention mechanism is used to carry out machine
translation tasks, which generate great results. Since then, the Attention mechanism
has become a popular research point.

Input
Apprentissage machine

21

Output
Transformer

machine learning

• As we know, ELMo uses LSTM instead of Transformer. If ELMO uses Transformer for feature
extraction, Bert may be far less popular than now. In addition, the capability of ELMo that
uses bidirectional stitching may be weaker than that of Bert integration. However, this is
only a suspicion raised by inference, and no specific experiment is available to illustrate this
point.

Reference: Attention is All You Need
22

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The layer structures in an encoder are the same, but they do not share parameters. Each
layer can be divided into two sub-layers. The output dimension d_model of each sub-layer
is 512.
• Sentences input from the encoder first pass through a self-attention layer which helps the
encoder focus on other words of the input sentence when encoding a word.
• The output of the self-attention layer is transferred to the feedforward neural network.
Feedforward neural networks corresponding to words in each position are completely the
same. (Another interpretation is a one-dimensional CNN in which a layer of window is a
word.)
• The decoder also has a self-attention layer and a feedforward layer of the encoder. In
addition, there is an attention layer between the two layers, which are used to focus on the
related part of the input sentence (similar to the attention function of the Seq2Seq model).

Transformer Implementation: Obtaining Input
⚫

Each input word is converted into a word vector through embedding, and then the word vector is added
to the position embedding of each word to obtain a representation vector X of each word. Finally, each
word is embedded into a 512-dimensional vector.

Word Embedding
⚫

Word Embedding can be obtained in a plurality of manners, for example, it can be obtained
through pre-training by using an algorithm such as Word2Vec or GloVe or through training in a
Transformer model.

28

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Positional Encoding
⚫

For Transformer, all words in a sentence are input into the network for processing at the same time. The sequence
information is lost when they are input. Transformer has to perform additional processing to inform the relative
position of each word. One of the solutions is positional encoding mentioned in the paper. The code that can
represent the position information is added to the input so that the network knows the position and sequence of
each word.

⚫

In a word, positional encoding provides the code of the relative position of a word in a sentence, which enables
Transformer to retain the position information of the word.
𝑃𝐸(𝑝𝑜𝑠,2𝑖) = sin(𝑝𝑜𝑠/100002𝑖/𝑑𝑚𝑜𝑑𝑒𝑙 )
𝑃𝐸(𝑝𝑜𝑠,2𝑖+1) = cos(𝑝𝑜𝑠/100002𝑖/𝑑𝑚𝑜𝑑𝑒𝑙 )
pos represents a position of a word in a sentence, d represents a dimension of PE (same as word Embedding), 2i

represents an even dimension, and 2i+1 represents an odd dimension (that is, 2i ≤ d and 2i+1 ≤ d).

29

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Using this formula to calculate the PE will:
▫ Enable the PE to adapt to sentences longer than all sentences in the training set.
▫ Enable the model to easily calculate the relative position. For the spacing k of a fixed
length, PE(pos+k) can be calculated by using PE(pos).

Self-Attention Mechanism
⚫

What is self-attention mechanism?

⚫

For example, the following sentence is the input sentence we want to translate:


⚫

The animal didn't cross the street because it was too tired.

What does "it" mean in this sentence? Does it refer to "street" or "animal"? This is a simple
problem for humans, but not for algorithms.

⚫

When a model processes the word "it", the self-attention mechanism allows "it" to be
associated with "animal".

31

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• If you are familiar with RNN, recall how it maintains hidden layers. The RNN combines the
representations of all the previous words/vectors that it has processed with the current
word/vector that it is processing. The self-attention mechanism integrates the
understanding of all related words into the words we are dealing with.
• When we encode the word "it" in encoder #5 (the top encoder in the stack), the attention
mechanism focuses on "The Animal" and encodes part of its representation into the code of
"it“.

Self-Attention Calculation
⚫

First, use vectors to calculate self-attention and then see how it is implemented with matrices.

⚫

The first step in calculating self-attention is to generate three vectors from the input vectors of
each encoder. That is, for each word, a query vector, a key vector, and a value vector need to be
created.

• The three vectors are created by multiplying the three weight matrices by word
embedding. These new vectors have smaller dimensions than those of word embedding
vectors. Their dimensions are 64, while those of word embedding and encoder
input/output vectors are 512. A smaller dimension is used as required by the architecture
to keep most of the calculations of multi-head attention unchanged.
• X1 is multiplied by the WQ weight matrix to obtain q1, which is the query vector related to
the word. Eventually, a query vector, a key vector, and a value vector are created for each
word of the input sequence.
• What are the query vector, key vector, and value vector? They are abstract concepts that
help calculate and understand the attention mechanism.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The second step in calculating self-attention is to calculate the score. Suppose we're
calculating a self-attention vector for the first word "Apprentissage" in this example, we
need to score "Apprentissage " with each word in the input sentence. These scores
determine how much attention is paid to the rest of the sentence in the process of coding
the word "Apprentissage". These scores are calculated by the dot product of the key vector
of the scored words (all the words of the input sentence) and the query vector of "
Apprentissage." So if we're dealing with the self-attention of the word in the front, the first
score is the dot product of q1 and k1, and the second score is the dot product of q1 and k2.

• 8 is the square root of the dimension 64 of the key vector used in the paper, which makes
the gradient more stable. You can also use other values. 8 is the default value.
• The Softmax score determines the contribution of each word to the current encoding
position ("Apprentissage"). Obviously, word already in the position will get the highest
Softmax score, but sometimes focusing on another word related to the current word can
also help.

• Multiply each value vector by the Softmax score (this is to sum them up later). The intuition

representations (key vectors) of the word and representations (query vectors) of the

to the first word in our example) is obtained.

• In order to further improve the self-attention layer, a mechanism called "multi-head"

• This mechanism improves the performance of the attention layer.

Attention Layer Performance Improvement

The performance of the attention layer is improved in two aspects: The model's ability to focus on different
positions is extended and it gives multiple "representation subspaces" of the attention layer.

41

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• To improve the performance of the attention layer, the paper added the "multi-headed"
attention mechanism. It improves the performance in two aspects: First, the model's ability
to focus on different positions is extended. In the example, although each code is more or
less embodied in z1, it may be dominated by the actual word itself. If we translate a
sentence, for example, "The animal didn't cross the street because it was too tired", we
want to know which word "it" refers to. In this case, the "multi-headed" attention
mechanism of the model will work. 2. It gives multiple "representation subspaces" of the
attention layer. For the "multi-headed" attention mechanism, there are multiple
query/key/value weight matrix sets (Transformer uses eight attention heads, and there are
eight matrix sets for each encoder/decoder). Each of these sets is randomly initialized, and
after training, each set is used to project an input word embedding (or a vector from a
lower encoder/decoder) into different representation subspaces.

• Under the "multi-headed" attention mechanism, an independent query/key/value weight
matrix is retained for each head, resulting in different query/key/value matrices. As before,
we multiply X by the WQ/WK/WV matrices to generate the query/key/value matrices.
• If we do the same self-attention calculation as above, we will get eight different Z matrices
with only eight different weight matrix operations.
• This poses a challenge to us. The feedforward layer does not require eight matrices. It
requires only one matrix (consisting of the representation vector of each word). So we need
a way to compress these eight matrices into one. What should we do?

• Differences between the decoder and encoder.

Masked Multi-Head Attention

First Multi-Head Attention
⚫

The first multi-head attention of the decoder block uses the Masked operation because
translation is performed in sequence. That is, the (i+1)th word can be translated only after the
ith word is translated. The Masked operation can prevent the ith word from knowing the

information following the (i+1)th word.

53

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

Second Multi-Head Attention
⚫

The second multi-head attention of the decoder block does not change greatly. The main
difference is that the K and V matrices of self-attention are not calculated based on the output
of the upper layer, but are calculated based on the encoding information matrix C of the

encoder.
⚫

K and V are calculated based on the encoding information matrix C output by the encoder, and
Q is calculated based on the output Z of the upper layer. Other calculation methods are the
same as those described above.

⚫

The advantage of this method is that each word can use the information about all words in the
encoder when being processed by the decoder.

54

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Now, we have learned most of the encoder concepts and how decoders work. Let's move
on to the details of the decoder. The encoder starts working by processing the input
sequence. The output of the top-layer encoder is converted into an attention vector set
containing vectors K (key vector) and V (value vector). These vectors will be used by each
decoder for its own "encoding-decoding attention layer", which helps the decoder focus on
appropriate positions of the input sequence.

and positional encoding is added to those
decoders to represent the position of each

word.

56

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The representation modes of the self-attention layer in the decoders are different from
those of encoders. In the decoders, the self-attention layer is allowed only to process the
front positions in the output sequence. Before Softmax is used, positions following them
are hidden (set to -inf). The "encoding-decoding attention layer" works virtually like a multihead self-attention layer, except that it creates a query matrix at the layer below it and
obtains a key/value matrix from the output of the encoder.

58

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• The decoding component outputs a real number vector at last. How do we turn floating
point numbers into a word? This is what the linear transformation layer does, which is
followed by the Softmax layer. The linear transformation layer is a simple fully connected
neural network. It can project the vector generated by the decoding component to a vector
that is much larger than the linear transformation layer and called logits. Suppose our
model learns 10,000 different English words (the "output vocabulary" of our model) from
the training set. The logits vector has a length of 10,000 cells with each cell corresponding
to the score of a word. The next Softmax layer turns those scores into probabilities (all
positive numbers, upper limit 1.0). The cell with the highest probability is selected, and its
corresponding word is used as the output of this time step.

⚫

We expect the model to output the correct translation after training. If it is already in the training set, it
is not an appropriate assessment indicator.
63

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

• Each position (word) gets a probability, even if it is unlikely to be the output of that time
step. This is a useful property of Softmax, which can help with model training.
• The model generates only one output at a time. Assume that the model selects only the
words with the highest probability and discards the remaining words. This method is called
greedy decoding. Another way to complete the task is to retain the two words with top two
probabilities (for example, I and a). Next, run the model twice. One assumption is that the
output of the first position is word "I", and another assumption is that the output of the
first position is word "me". No matter which assumption generates fewer deviations, the
two translation results with top two probabilities are retained. Then, this step is repeated
for the second and third positions. This method is referred to as beam search. In our
example, the beam width is 2 (the results of two beams are retained, such as the first and
second positions), and the results of two beams are returned (top_beams is also 2). These
parameters can be preset.

Dense Model and Sparse Model
⚫

Model size is a key factor in model performance. As Transformer-based AI models evolve, the number of
parameters is increasing, which enhances model performance. If all parameters are involved in during
training and inference computation (i.e. using most dense matrices), the required computational power
will also increase. Therefore, the inference cost of such large, dense models is relatively high.

⚫

Is it possible to increase the number of parameters without significantly increasing the computational
demand?

⚫

MoE uses a subset of parameters for computation, meaning that only a small portion of parameters is
non-zero. This sparse matrix reduces the need for compute resources in model training and inference,
accelerating computation.

65

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

MoE — GShard
⚫

GShard, released by Google, applied MoE to the
Transformer model.

⚫

The Transformer encoder layer comprises two
consecutive layers: a self-attention layer

⚫

The encoder/decoder consists of
multiple blocks. The MoE layer
replaces a feed-forward network
(FFN) layer every other block.

followed by a position-wise feed-forward layer.
The decoder contains a third cross-attention
layer that focuses on the encoder's output.
Transformers are sparsely scaled with conditional
computation by replacing every other feedforward layer with a position-wise MoE layer.

67

•

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

In the previous MoE architecture, each sample is assigned to a different expert, whereas
tokens are assigned to a different expert in a Transformer architecture.

GShard — Top-K Gating
⚫

The gating network may employ top-K gating, where
only the top-K experts with the highest probabilities
are selected for computation for each input token. In

GShard, K is set to 2, meaning top-2 experts are
chosen.
⚫

The gating function in GShard meets two criteria:

68

•



Load balancing; and



Efficient large-scale parallel computing capabilities.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

The MoE layer is designed to sparsely activate an expert for a given token. A simple
solution is to select the top-k experts based on the softmax probability distribution.
However, this often leads to a load imbalance during training because most tokens are
assigned to a small number of experts, and these high-load experts accumulate large
input buffers, impacting training speed. Meanwhile, many other experts remain
undertrained. A better gating function design is needed to evenly distribute the
processing load among all experts.

•

Sequential execution of the gating function can achieve load balancing. In practice,
however, a sequential approach would underutilize computational resources for a
system with millions of tokens and thousands of experts. An efficient parallel
implementation of the gating function is necessary to leverage multiple devices.

The DeepSeek-V3 network still runs on the MoE
structure, but this has been optimized.

DeepSeek-V3 Technical Report

72

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

⚫

Traditional prediction and inference are slow
because they generate tokens one by one,
requiring significant interaction with GPU
memory for each token prediction.
Additionally, individual predictions are good
for optimal local solutions, but can impact
overall performance.

⚫

In the decoding phase, the model aims to
predict multiple future tokens at once
through multiple sequential modules.
Specifically, generating multiple subsequent
tokens in one operation in the training phase
enables concurrent multi-position learning,
enhancing sample utilization and training
efficiency. This exponentially increases
inference speed because multiple tokens can
be generated at once.

DeepSeek-V3 Engineering Innovation — FP8 Training

⚫

Mixed precision policy:

73



To enhance training speed, compute-intensive operators (such as Fprop, Dgrad, and Wgrad) are executed using FP8
calculations.



Precision-sensitive modules (such as the vector layer, output layer, gating module, and attention module) still maintain
BF16/FP32 precision to ensure any loss of precision is within an acceptable range.



The optimizer momentum utilizes BF16, while the primary weight parameters and gradients are kept in FP32 format.

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

DeepSeek-V3 Engineering Innovation — DualPipe
⚫

In traditional pipeline parallelism, each compute node performs a portion of the calculations (such as forward propagation and
backward propagation). After the calculations are complete, the results wait to be transferred to the next GPU. Since each
calculation waits for communication to finish before each node can proceed, the following node must wait for cross-node
communication, leading to underutilized resources. This idle time is known as a pipeline bubble.

1F1B. The white cell represents the idle time of each
compute card.
⚫

DualPipe:


Each chunk is divided into four components: attention, all-to-all dispatch, MLP, and all-to-all combine.



DualPipe employs bidirectional pipeline scheduling, which feeds micro-batches from both ends of the pipeline simultaneously and a significant
portion of communications can be fully overlapped.
8 PP ranks and 20 micro-batches

Copyright © Huawei Technologies Co., Ltd. All rights reserved.

DeepSeek Knowledge Distillation
⚫

Knowledge distillation is a technique that transfers knowledge from a large, complex model (teacher model, e.g.,
DeepSeek-R1-671B) to a smaller, efficient model (student model, e.g., Qwen-7B).

Distilling the Knowledge in a Neural Network

⚫

DeepSeek-R1 generates 800,000 data records as supervision data.

⚫

SFT is performed on open-source small models such as Qwen and Llama, instead of using reinforcement learning.

⚫

The performance of a 32B/70B model is close to that of OpenAI o1-mini. For example, DeepSeek-R1-Distill-Qwen32B achieves 72.6% Pass@1 on AIME 2024.

Summary
⚫

The pioneering idea of Transformer overturns the idea of equaling sequence

modeling to RNN, and is now widely used in various fields of NLP. Currently, language
models such as GPT and BERT that are widely used in NLP services use the
Transformer architecture.
⚫

This chapter describes the attention mechanism and the core technologies of
Transformer, including why the attention mechanism is introduced, specific principles
of attention, structure of Transformer, self-attention mechanism, encoder, and
decoder. In addition, this chapter analyzes the training process of Transformer.
